A  BRIEF  HISTORY  OF  THE   CHURCH 

Although,   the  earliest  record  of  the  First 
United  Methodist  Church  of  Norwood  is  dated  1825,  it 
is  believed  that  Methodists  were  active  and  conducting 
camp  meetings  before  that.     George  Kendall  deeded 
five  acres  of  land  (as  Norwood  was  then  known)   for 
the  purpose  of  building  a  place  of  worship .     That 
first  church  was  built  between   1820  and   1825  of  logs 
with  a  large  fireplace  at  one  end  and  a  pulpit  at  the 
other. 

The  Center  Circuit  formed  in   1833,   as  a  part  of 
the  South  Carolina  Conference,   consisted  of  Norwood, 
Bethel,   Randall,    Salem,    Stony  Hill  and  Albemarle.      In 
1847,   the  churches  in  Stanly  County  were  put  in  the 
newly  formed  Albemarle  Circuit,    still  a  part  of  the 
South  Carolina  Conference.      In   1870,    South  Carolina 
gave  up  the  churches  west  of  the  Pee  Dee  River. 

In  the   1880's  the  present  church  building  was 
erected  with  Frank  Ivey,   Whitman  Smith,   Eli  Lentz, 
Thomas  Colson,   Jr.,   Eli  Shankle  and  T.A.   Lowder 
making  up  the  Building  Committee.     Mr.   Ivey  served 
as  Building  Contractor.     The  curved  beam  ceiling 
which  excited  builders  and  engineers  was  Mr.   Ivey's 
concept  and  remains  in  place  today  along  with  the 
sills  donated  by  Jacob  and  Eli  Shankle,   hewed  by 
Jacob  with  a  broad  axe. 

In   1890,   Norwood  was  removed  from  the  Albemarle 
Circuit  by  the  Western  North  Carolina  Conference  and, 
along  with  Randall,   Rehobeth,   Mt.    Zion  and  Cedar 
Grove,   became  the  Norwood  Circuit  in  the  Salisbury 
District. 

By   1894  a  new  Circuit  parsonage  in  Norwood   was 
ready- valued  at  $1100  with  a  garden  and  four  years 
later,   a  stable.     A  classroom  was  authorized  to  be 
built  to  the  church  in   1910.     Committee:     J.   F.    Shinn, 
J.   D.   Lee,    V.   L.    Shankle  and  E.   M.   Harris.     A  light- 
ing system   was  installed  in   1912.     Committee:      B.   F. 
Ivey,   G.   T.   Dunlap,   and  C.   A.   Lentz. 

The  cemetery  was  moved  from  the  church  lot  to 
the  Town  Cemetery  in   1915.     In   1917  the  church  was 
renovated,   a  Sunday  school  annex  added,   the  tower 
rebuilt,    a  new  bell  installed  and  the  whole  brick 

-B- 


veneered.     There  was  new  lighting  and  hot  air  furnace. 
Cost  of  renovations  was  $6500.     In   1921,   Norwood  be- 
came a  separate  Station  with  a  full-time  pastor,   C.   M. 
Short . 

In   1949  a  drive  began  which  culminated  in  another 
renovation  of  the  church  and  a  new  parsonage. 
Committee:     D.E.   Lefler,   L.E.   Dry,   J.C.   Guffy,   J.L. 
Lee  and  M.V.   Lowder.      In   1960,   the  churches  in 
Stanly,   Union  and  Anson  were  made  the  new 
Albemarle  District.     In   1976  new  pews  were  bought, 
carpet  laid  and  the  sanctuary  refurbished.     In   1985, 
the  Fellowship  Hut  and  kitchen  were  enlarged  with  the 
addition  of  two  restrooms. 

Women  in  the  Church  have  been  active  during 
these  years,    growing  from  a  local  Ladies  Aid  Society 
to  the  Women's  Foreign  Missionary  Society  that  became 
the  Women's  Society  of  Christian  Service,    that  in  turn, 
became  the  present  United  Methodist  Women. 

Members  of  the  Church  have  gone  out  as  Minis- 
ters,  Deaconnesses.   Directors  of  Christian  Education 
and  one  missionary  to  China,   Miss  Louise  Avett.     Our 
Church  has  a  fine  heritage  that  will  continue  as  our 
members  grow  in  Christian  love  by  the  grace  of  God.

APPRECIATION 

The  First  United  Methodist  Church  would 
like  to  thank  and  express  its  sincere  appre-

have  been  possible.

Appetizers 


Appetizers  are  those  treats  that  can  be  served  either  at  the  start  of  a 
meal  or  at  a  reception  or  open  house.  Listed  below  are  quick  appetizers 
that  can  be  served  anytime  with  crackers,  thin  sliced  toasted  bread  or 
potato  chips: 

1.  Caviar  flavored  with  onion  juice. 

2.  Cream  cheese  with  chipped  chutney  and  dash  of  curry  powder. 

3.  Lobster  tail  moistened  with  lemon  juice. 

4.  Almonds  or  pecans  roasted  and  chopped,  then  mixed  with  anchovy 
paste. 

5.  Cream  cheese  with  chopped  pickle. 

6.  Chicken  livers  minced  and  moistened  with  mayonnaise. 

7.  Cheese  squares  with  olive  attached  by  toothpick. 

8.  Liverwurst  with  pistachio  nuts. 

9.  Sardines  with  caviar  paste. 

10.  Minced  eggs  with  anchovies. 

11.  Cream  cheese  and  horseradish. 

12.  Cream  cheese  and  anchovy  paste  with  grated  onion. 

13.  Herring  squares  mashed  in  its  own  juice  with  dash  of  vinegar  and 
Tabasco  sauce. 

14.  Peanut  butter  and  bacon  toasted  on  dark  bread. 

15.  Deviled  ham  with  chopped  onions  and  Spanish  olives. 
16    Stilton  cheese  moistened  with  Port  wine. 

17.  Shrimp  flavored  with  French  dressing. 

18.  Caviar  mixed  with  cream  cheese  with  dash  of  Worcestershire  sauce. 

19.  Peanuts  roasted,  crushed  and  mixed  with  anchovy  paste. 

20.  Sardine  slices  topped  with  chopped  olives. 

21.  Pimento  cheese  mixed  with  a  dash  of  horseradish. 

22.  Minced  shrimp  with  onion  juice. 

23.  Cream  cheese  with  dash  of  Worcestershire  sauce  and  chives.

APPETIZERS,  RELISHES  &  PICKLES 


SAUSAGE-CHEESE  TIDBITS 

1  lb.  sausage  3  c.  Bisquick 

1  lb.  sharp  Cheddar  cheese 

Mix  all  ingredients  well;  form  into  small  balls.  Bake  at  325° 
for  about  20  minutes  or  until  done. 

Pat  Reid 

SAUSAGE  BALLS 

4  c.  Bisquick  baking  mix  10  to  16  oz.  shredded  Cheddar 

1/2  lb.  sausage  cheese 

Mix  well  and  roll  into  small  balls.  Put  on  ungreased  cookie 
sheet.  Bake  for  15  minutes.  May  be  frozen  before  cooked;  layer  balls 
with  waxed  paper. 

Susie  Bowers 

SPICED  NUTS 

1  egg  white  1  Tbsp.  cinnamon 

2  2/3  c.  pecans  or  walnuts  3/4  tsp.  salt 
3/4  c.  sugar  1  tsp.  water 

Slightly  beat  egg  white  and  combine  water.  Add  nuts,  toss  to 
coat.  Add  sugar,  cinnamon  and  salt.  Add  to  nuts,  toss  until  all  are 
well  coated.  Place  in  single  layer  on  lightly  greased  baking  sheet. 
Bake  in  300°  oven  for  20  to  25  minutes.  Remove  and  cool  on  wax  paper. 
Break  up  large  clusters.     Makes  approximately  4  1/2  cups. 

Faye  Holton  Hart 

BUTTERED  PECANS 

1/2  stick  butter  or  margarine  salt  to  taste 

4  c.  pecans 

Melt  margarine.  Add  pecans  and  stir  well.  Toast  15  minutes  in 
400°  oven.     Watch  closely  and  stir  if  needed.     Add  salt  to  taste. 

Lela  Maude  Lowder 

SUGAR  COATED  PEANUTS 

2  c.  raw  peanuts  1/2  c.  water 

1  c.  sugar 


63786  -1- 


APPETIZERS,  RELISHES  &  PICKLES 


Bring     sugar  and  water  to  boil.     Add  peanuts.     Pour  on  ungreased 
pan.     Bake  for  5  to  10  minutes  at  350°,  stirring  every  5  minutes. 

Susie  Bowers 


BAR-B-QUE  MEAT  BALLS 


1  lb.  ground  beef 
1/2  c.  milk 

Sauce: 

1/2  c.  catsup 

1  tsp.  salt  and  pepper 

1  1/2  tsp.  Worcestershire 

sauce 
1/8  c.  vinegar 


1  c.  bread  crumbs 


3  Tbsp.  sugar 

1/2  c.  water 

1/2  c.  green  pepper,  chopped 

1/2  c.  onion,  chopped 


Mix  ground  beef,  milk  and  bread  crumbs.  Form  into  balls.  Mix 
ingredients  for  sauce  and  pour  over  balls.  Bake  about  45  minutes  at 
375°. 

Evelyn  Guffy 


MEAT  BALLS 


1  lb.  ground  chuck  steak  or  1 

lb.  lean  hamburger 
1  c.  cracker  crumbs 
1/2  c.  catsup 
1  c.  chopped  onion 
1  tsp.  black  pepper 


1  tsp.  salt 
1/4  c.  vinegar 

3  Tbsp.  brown  sugar 
1/2  c.  catsup 

2  tsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 


Mix  ground  chuck  or  hamburger,  cracker  crumbs  and  1/2  cup  catsup 
together.  Shape  into  small  balls.  Place  in  baking  dish  and  pour  over 
them  a  mixture  made  of  1/2  cup  catsup,  onion,  pepper,  salt,  vinegar, 
brown  sugar,  catsup  and  Worcestershire  sauce.  Cook  in  moderate  oven 
until  meat  balls  are  cooked  through. 

Nell  Colson 

SPINACH  DIP 


8  oz.  sour  cream 
1  pkg.  Knorr  vegetable  soup 
mix 


1  pkg.  frozen  chopped  spinach, 

thawed  and  drained 
1  c.  mayonnaise  or  to  taste 


Mix      all   ingredients   and   refrigerate  overnight.      May   be   used   for 
sandwiches  on  pumpernickel  bread. 

Helen  L.  Garner 

CREAM  CHEESE  SPREAD 


1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese 
1  pkg.  dried  beef,  chopped 


1  small  onion,  chopped 

1  tsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 


APPETIZERS,  RELISHES  &  PICKLES 


Chop  beef  and  onion  and  combine  with  other  ingredients.  Refrig- 
erate and  serve  on  crackers. 

John  W.  Thompson 

CHEESE  BALL 

2  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese  1  envelope  Hidden  Valley 

1  c.  grated  Cheddar  cheese  buttermilk  dressing  mix 

chopped  nuts 

Mix  cream  cheese,  Cheddar  cheese  and  dressing  mix.  Shape  into 
ball  or  log  and  roll  in  nuts. 

Lisa  Davis 

VEGETABLE-CHEESE  BALL  OR  DSP 

2  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese  1/4  c.  finely  chopped  green 

1  c.  finely  chopped  pecans  pepper 

2  Tbsp.  finely  chopped  onion  1  Tbsp.  seasoned  salt 

1  (8  1/2  oz.)  can  crushed  (McCormick  preferred) 

pineapple 

Thoroughly  dram  pineapple,  squeezing  out  all  liquid  possible. 
Cream  cheese  and  pineapple.  Add  other  ingredients.  Form  into  ball  or 
place  in  dish  for  dip.     Serve  with  salted  crackers. 

Gail  T.  Bunn 

CHEESE  BALL 

8  oz.  cream  cheese  1  small  jar  dried  beef, 

1/2  pkg.  Cracker  Barrel  sharp  chopped 

Cheddar  cheese  green  onions,  grated 

Combine  ingredients  and  shape  into  ball.  Roll  in  chopped 
pecans. 

Susie  Bowers 

CHEESE  BALL 

1  (3  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese  1  pkg.  Hidden  Valley 

1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese  buttermilk  salad  dressing 

mix 
chopped  pecans 

Mix  both  packages  of  cream  cheese  with  salad  dressing  mix:  form 
into  one  large  ball  or  two  small  ones.  Roll  in  chopped  nuts  and  wrap 
in  plastic  wrap. 

Margaret  Lisenby

APPETIZERS,  RELISHES  &  PIC 


KLES  f 


DEVILED  BISCUITS 


1  (8  oz.)  can  refrigerated 

biscuits 
1/4  c.  margarine 


1  (4  1/2  oz.)  can  deviled  ham 
1/4  c.  grated  Parmesan  or 
sharp  Cheddar  cheese 


Snip  biscuits  into  quarters.  Arrange  in  two  round  8-inch  baking 
pans.  Heat  together  margarine  and  deviled  ham,  stirring  until  blended. 
Pour  ham  mixture  evenly  over  biscuit  pieces.  Sprinkle  with  cheese. 
Bake  at  400°  for  15  minutes.  Serve  hot.  Makes  40  appetizers  or  serve 
with  scrambled  eggs. 

Margaret  Lisenby 


SQUASH  RELISH 


6  large  yellow  squash 
4  large  onions 
3  sweet  peppers 
2  hot  peppers 
1  c.  cold  water 


1/4  c.  salt 
2  1/2  c.  vinegar 
2  1/2  c.  sugar 
3/4  tsp.  turmeric 
1  Tbsp.  celery  seed 


Grind  squash,  onions  and  peppers  in  food  chopper.  Cover  with 
salt  and  cold  water.  Let  stand  1  hour.  Drain  and  rinse.  Bring  to 
boil  vinegar,  sugar,  turmeric  and  celery  seed.  Add  squash,  peppers  and 
onions  and  boil  10  minutes.  Put  in  pint  jars  (sterilized  and  hot)  and 
seal.     Yields  6  to  7  pints. 

Miriam  J.  Sims 


QUICK  CORN  RELISH 


1/4  c.  sugar 

1/2  c.  vinegar 

1/2  tsp.  salt 

1/2  tsp.  celery  seed 

1/2  tsp.  mustard  seed 


1  can  whole  kernel  corn, 
drained 

2  Tbsp.  chopped  green  pepper 
1  Tbsp.  chopped  pimento 

1  Tbsp.  minced  onion 


Combine  sugar,  vinegar,  salt,  celery  seed,  mustard  seed  and  corn 
in  saucepan;  bring  to  a  boil.  Boil  for  2  minutes.  Combine  with 
remaining     ingredients.     Chill.     Flavor     improves     on  standing.     Yield: 

about  1  2/3  cups. 

Mildred  Lee 


12  green  peppers 
12  red  peppers 
4  hot  peppers 
1  bunch  celery 
12  large  apples 


SWEET  PEPPER  RELISH 

2  lb.  onions 

1  1/2  qt.  vinegar 

2  lb.  sugar 
2  Tbsp.  salt 
1  qt.  water 


Peel     and     chop    apples  and  celery.     Grind  onions  and  peppers  in 


-4- 


APPETIZERS,  RELISHES  &  PICKLES 


food  chopper.  Dissolve  salt  in  1  quart  water.  Mix  all  ingredients  and 
let  stand  1/2  hour.  Drain.  After  draining,  add  sugar  and  vinegar. 
Cook  for  1  1/2  hours.  Seal  in  hot  sterilized  pint  jars.  Makes  8 
pints. 

Miriam  J.  Sims 


KOSHER  DILL  PICKLES 


3  qt.  water 

20  to  25  medium  cucumbers, 

soaked  in  ice  water 

overnight 
1  qt.  vinegar 
1/8  tsp.  alum 


1/2  hot  pepper 

1  clove  garlic 

2  beads  diii  or  1  tsp.  dill 
seed 

1  grape  leaf  per  jar 
1/2  c.  salt 


Pack  in  hot  jars;  grape,   leaf  on  top.     Seal. 

Ruth  Clayton 

BOB'S  DILL  PICKLES 


2  1/2  lb.  small  cucumbers 
fresh  dill  heads  or  dill  seed 
garlic  cloves 
hot  red  peppers 
3/4  c.  pickling  salt 
4  c.  cider  vinegar 


3  qt.  water 
whole  mustard  seed 
alum 

sterilized  and  hot  qt  jars  (5 
or  6) 


Wash  cucumbers  and  cut  off  blossom  end.  To  each  quart  jar  add  1 
large  dill  head  or  1  teaspoon  dill  seed,  1  clove  garlic,  1  small  hot 
pepper,  1/2  teaspoon  mustard  seed  and  1/8  teaspoon  alum.  Pack  cucum- 
bers in  jars,  leaving  1/2-inch  head  space.  In  gallon  container  combine 
salt,  vinegar  and  water  and  bring  to  boil.  Pour  mixture  over  cucumbers 
leaving  1/2-inch  head  space  and  adjust  lids  tightly.  Process  in 
boiling  water  bath  10  minutes. 

Bob  Sims 

CUCUMBER  CINNAMON  RINGS 


large  cucumbers  (make  2  gal. 

rings) 
2  c.  dehydrated  lime 
8  1/2  c.  water  or  more 
1  c.  vinegar-water 
1  bottle  red  food  coloring 


1  Tbsp.  salt 

2  c.  vinegar 
2  c.  water 
10  c.  sugar 

8  sticks  cinnamon 

1  pkg.  red  hot  candies  or  1  c. 


Peel  cucumbers.  Cut  into  rings  and  remove  seeds.  Put  2  gallons 
of  rings  in  large  crock  or  enamel  pot.  Add  2  cups  lime  and  water, 
enough  to    cover.     Let  stand  24  hours.     Drain. 

Wash  rings  well  in  cool  water  and  cover  with  cool  water.  Let 
soak  3  hours  and  dram.  Add  1  cup  vinegar,  1  bottle  red  food  coloring 
and  1  tablespoon  salt  with  water  to  cover.  Heat  and  simmer  on  low  heat 
for  2     hours.     Drain. 


63786 


-5- 


APPETIZERS,  RELISHES  &  PICKLES 


Make  syrup  with  2  cups  vinegar,  2  cups  water,  10  cups  sugar  and 
1  package  or  1  cup  red  hot  candy.  Bring  to  boil.  Pour  over  cucumbers. 
Cover  and  let  stand  overnight.  Drain.  Reheat  syrup  to  boiling.  Put 
rings  in  jars.     Pour  boiling  syrup  over  them  and  seal. 

Nell  Colson

Salads 


Additions  and  Garnishes 


Tips  for  Tossed  Salads 


Slice  hard-cooked  eggs 

Radishes 

Chopped  green  or  ripe  olives 

Nut  meats 

Pimento 

Green  pepper 

Sardines 

Anchovies 

Slivered  cheeses 

Julienned  ham 

Chicken 

Grated  carrots 

Cubed  celery 

Onions  -  pickled,  grated  or  pearl  onions 

Tomatoes,  sliced  and  dipped  in  finely 

chopped  parsley  or  chives 
Capers 
Dwarf  tomatoes    stuffed    with    cottage 

cheese 
Fresh  herbs  -  sprigs  or  chopped 
Mint  leaves 

Cooked  beets,  cut  into  shapes  or  sticks 
Lemon   slices   with   pinked   edges   and 

dipped  in  chopped  parsley 
Raw  cauliflower 


Always  handle  salad  greens  with  care. 

Wash  well,  drain  and  dry  greens  before 
storingxhill  well  before  using. 

To  core  lettuce,  smack  head  stem  end 
down  on  counter  top.  Then  twist  the  core 
out. 

It  is  better  to  tear  greens  into  bite-sized 
pieces  to  avoid  bruising  with  knife. 

Don't  cut  up  tomatoes  for  a  tossed  salad 
since  their  juices  thin  the  dressing  and 
wilt  the  greens.  Using  them  only  for 
garnishing  the  salad  bowl. 

Select  only  firm,  hard,  green  cucumbers. 
The  skin  should  have  a  slight  sheen,  but 
if  it  is  highly  polished,  it  is  probably 
waxed  and  should  be  removed. 

Use  wild  greens  such  as  dandelion,  sorrel 
or  winter  cress  for  a  different  flavor  and 
texture  in  tossed  salads. 


About  Potato  Salad- 


Soup  Accompaniments- 


Potato  salad  is  best  made  from  potatoes 
cooked  in  their  jackets  and  peeled  and 
marinated  while  still  warm.  Small  red 
waxy  potatoes  hold  their  shape  when 
sliced  or  diced  and  do  not  absorb  an 
excessive  amount  of  dressing  or  become 
mushy. 


Clear  Soups  -  crisp  crackers,  cheese 
pastry,  cheese-spread  toast  strips. 

Cream  Soups  -  cheese  popcorn,  seeded 
crackers,  pretzels,  pickles  and  olives. 

Chowders  and  Meat  Soups  -  Melba  toast, 
sour  pickles,  oyster  crackers,  bread 
sticks,  relishes,  toasted  garlic  bread.

SOUPS,  SALADS  &  SAUCES 


HOT  POTATO  SOUP 


4  c.  diced  potatoes 
1  medium  onion,  chopped 
4  Tbsp.  vegetable  oil 
1  1/2  c.  chopped  cooked 
chicken 


1  c.  chicken  broth 

2  tsp.  parsley  flakes 
2  tsp.  salt 

1  (13  oz.)  tall  can  Pet 
evaporated  milk 


Coat  potatoes  and  onions  with  oil  in  hot  saucepan.  Add  chicken, 
chicken  broth,  parsley  and  salt.  Heat  to  boiling.  Lower  heat.  Cover. 
Simmer  until  potatoes  are  tender,  about  30  minutes.  Stir  in  Pet  milk. 
Serve  HOT.    Makes  6  servings,  1  cup  each. 

Polly  Mabry 


BROCCOLI  SOUP 


3/4  c.  chopped  celery 
1/4  c.  chopped  onion 
2  Tbsp.  oleo,  melted 
2  (10  oz.)  pkg.  chopped 
broccoli 


2  c.  chicken  broth 
1  c.  milk 
1/2  tsp.  salt 
1/4  tsp.  pepper 


Saute  celery  and  onions  in  oleo  in  skillet.  Add  broccoli  and 
broth.  Bring  to  a  boil.  Cover  and  simmer  5  minutes.  Cool.  Place  in 
blender  1/2  at  a  time  and  mix  well.  Pour  into  saucepan  and  stir  in 
milk,  salt  and  pepper.  Place  on  low  heat  until  completely  heated. 
Makes  about  5  1/2  cups. 

Miriam  J.  Sims

1  bunch  celery 


1  pod  green  bell  pepper 
1  large  can  tomatoes 


Cut  vegetables.  Cover  with  water  and  boil  10  minutes  or  until 
vegetables  are  soft.  Eat  over  rice.  You  may  add  Parmesan  cheese  and 
soy  sauce  if  desired. 

Mary  Frances  Colson

STRAWBERRY  SALAD 


1  1/2  c.  boiling  water 

2  pkg.  strawberry  jello 
1  to  1  1/2  pkg.  frozen 

strawberries 


1  c.  crushed  pineapple 
1/2  c.  pecans,  chopped 
1  c.  sour  cream 


Note:     A  little  Cool  Whip  may  be  added  to  sour  cream. 

Fix  jello  and  add  berries.  Chill  until  slightly  congealed.  Add 
pineapple  and  nuts  and  put  1/2  of  mixture  in  mold  or  Pyrex  pan.  Chill. 
When  set,  fold  sour  cream  into  remaining  mixture  and  pour  over  the 
jello  which  is  already  set.     Serves  12.

GREEN  SALAD 


2  boxes  lime  jello 

2  c.  hot  water 

1  small  jar  diced  pimento 

1  (3  oz.)  bar  cream  cheese 


1  small  can  crushed  pineapple 

1  c.  broken  pecans 

1  small  carton  whipped  topping 


Make  up  jello  with  hot  water.  Let  this  cool.  Mash  cream  cheese 
in  pineapple  and  heat  slowly  until  not  in  lumps.  Add  this  to  jello 
mixture.  Add  pimento,  nuts  and  whipped  topping.  Congeal  overnight. 
Serves  12  to  15. 

Margaret  Skidmore

BLENDER  CONGEALED  SALAD 


1  (16  oz.)  can  pears 
1  c.  juice  from  pears 
1  (3  oz.)  box  lime  gelatin 


1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese 
1  (8  oz.)  carton  lemon  yogurt 


Drain  pears.  Boil  1  cup  of  pear  juice  (add  enough  water  to  make 
1  cup,  if  necessary).  Dissolve  gelatin  in  boiling  juice,  cool  slight- 
ly, then  pour  into  blender  container.  Turn  on  blender  for  a  few 
seconds  at  a  medium  speed.  Add  pears  and  blend.  Add  cream  cheese  and 
yogurt  and  blend  until  light  in  color  and  thoroughly  blended.  Pour 
into  dish  and  refrigerate  until  firm.  May  also  use  lemon,  strawberry 
or  tropical  fruit  flavored  gelatin. 

Elisabeth  Penry

MOLDED  VEGETABLE  RELISH 


2  (3  oz.)  pkg.  lemon  or  lime 
gelatin 

1  1/2  tsp.  salt 

2  c.  boiling  water 
1  1/2  c.  cold  water 
4  Tbsp.  vinegar 


4  tsp.  grated  onion 

1  c.  shredded  cabbage 

1  c.  grated  carrot 

1/2  c.  sliced  celery 

6  Tbsp.  chopped  green  pepper 

1/4  c.  chopped  pimento 


Dissolve  gelatin  and  salt  in  boiling  water.  Put  into  casserole 
dish.  Add  cold  water,  vinegar  and  onion.  (Sliced  green  onion  can  be 
used     for     more     texture     and     taste.)     Chill  until  thickened. 

Fold  in  vegetables.  Chill  until  firm;  at  least  3  hours. 
Garnish   if      desired   with   olives,   carrot  or   radish   curls,   etc.      Yields   6 

to  8  generous  servings.

HOT  ORIENTAL  SALAD 


2  Tbsp.  salad  oil 

1  medium  onion,  sliced 

2  c.  sliced  fresh  mushrooms 
2  c.  sliced  celery 

2  green  peppers,  cut  into 

chunks 
1  (5  02.)  can  water  chestnuts, 

sliced  and  drained 
1  (6  oz.)  pkg.  snow  peas 


1/2  c.  chicken  broth  (maybe 

more) 
2  Tbsp.  cornstarch 

1  1/4  tsp.  salt 

2  Tbsp.  water 

2  Tbsp.  soy  sauce 

1  c.  bean  sprouts,  drained 

1  to  2  c.  cashews 


Heat  oil  in  large  skillet.  Add  onions,  celery,  peppers,  chest- 
nuts, pea  pods  and  mushrooms.  Stir-fry  over  high  heat  until  all  are 
well  coated  with  oil  and  crisp-tender.  Add  broth;  cover  and  cook  5 
minutes.  Meanwhile,  mix  cornstarch,  salt,  water  and  soy  sauce.  Stir 
until  smooth.  Stir  into  vegetables.  Add  more  broth  if  necessary. 
Stir  in  bean  sprouts  and  nuts.     Heat  through.     Serves  8. 

Carolyn  Trail

TEXAS  SLAW 


1  medium  cabbage,  grated 
1  medium  green  pepper,  finely 

chopped 
1  large  onion,  finely  chopped 
1  carrot,  grated 
1  c.  sugar 


1/2  c.  salad  oil 

1/2  c.  vinegar 

2  Tbsp.  chopped  parsley 

1  tsp.  salt 

1/2  tsp.  dry  mustard 

1/4  tsp.  pepper 


The  day  before  serving,  put  cabbage,  green  pepper,  onion  and 
carrot  in  mixing  bowl.  In  another  bowl,  combine  remaining  ingredients. 
Beat  until  smooth  and  blended.  Pour  dressing  over  vegetables  and  toss 
lightly.     Cover  and  refrigerate  overnight.     Serves  12. 

Mary  Jane  Komlos 


MARINATED  SLAW 


1  large  cabbage 

1  bell  pepper 

2  onions 
2  c.  sugar 

1  c.  vinegar 


3/4  c.  salad  oil 

1  tsp.  dry  mustard 

1  tsp.  celery  seed 

1  Tbsp.  salt 

1  Tbsp.  plus  1  tsp.  sugar 


Chop  cabbage,  peppers  and  onions  and  mix.  Add  2  cups  sugar  (I 
use  1  cup).  Place  remaining  ingredients  in  a  saucepan  and  bring  to 
boil.  Pour  boiled  mixture  over  cabbage.  Seal  in  airtight  container. 
Do  not  stir  or  uncover  for  at  least  4  hours.  Will  keep  in  refrigerator 
for  a  week  or  more. 

Lucy  A.  Lanier

CHICKEN  DIVAN 


2  c.  cooked  chicken 

1  pkg.  broccoli  spears  (frozen 

or  fresh) 
1  c.  grated  Cheddar  cheese 
1/4  c.  chopped  onions 


2/3  c.  heavy  cream 
1/2  c.  mayonnaise 
1/4  tsp.  Tabasco  sauce 
1/3  c.  Parmesan  cheese 
crumbs 


Spray  9  x  13-inch  dish,  spread  broccoli  over.  Add  chicken, 
onions  and  Cheddar  cheese.  Mix  together  mayonnaise,  cream  and  Tabasco 
sauce.  Pour  over  chicken-broccoli  mixture.  Sprinkle  with  Parmesan 
cheese,  then  sprinkle  with  crumbs.     Bake  at  350°  for  25  minutes. 

Ella  H.  Maner 


CHICKEN  DIVAN 


3  chicken  breasts  (whole) 
2  pkg.  frozen  broccoli 
1  can  cream  of  chicken  soup 
2/3  c.  mayonnaise 


1/3  c.  milk 

1/2  c.  grated  cheese 

1  tsp.  lemon  juice 

1/4  to  1/2  tsp.  curry  powder 


Cook  chicken  breasts  and  remove  meat.  Couk  broccoli  until 
almost  tender;  place  broccoli  and  chicken  in  alternate  layers  in 
casserole.  Combine  all  remaining  ingredients  and  pour  on  top.  Bake  30 
minutes  at  350°.     Serves  8. 

Note:    Reserve  some  cheese  and  place  on  top  with  bread  crumbs. 

Polly  Mabry 

CHICKEN  BROCCOLI  DIVINE 


4  chicken  breasts,  deboned 

1  onion,  sliced 

1  c.  diced  celery 

1  tsp.  salt  and  pepper 

1  pkg.  broccoli 

1  c.  mayonnaise 


1  tsp.  lemon  juice 

1  tsp.  curry  powder 

1  can  cream  of  chicken  soup 

1  c.  shredded  Cheddar  cheese 
1/4  stack  crackers,  crushed 

2  Tbsp.  butter 


Cook  chicken,  onion,  celery,  salt  and  pepper  until  chicken  is 
tender.  Line  the  bottom  of  a  large  casserole  dish  with  a  package  of 
broccoli  that  has  been  defrosted.  Lay  chicken  breasts  over  the  brocco- 
li. Mix  mayonnaise,  lemon  juice,  curry  powder  and  soup.  Spread 
mixture  over  chicken.  Top  with  a  mixture  ot  cheese,  cracker  crumbs  and 
butter.     Bake  in  350°  oven  for  30  minutes. 

Ginger  Colson

CHICKEN-BROCCOLI  QUICHE 


1  pkg.  frozen  chopped  broccoli 
1  c.  chopped  cooked  chicken 
1/2  c.  chopped  onion 
1  c.  shredded  Cheddar  cheese 
1/2  c.  Swiss  cheese 


3  eggs 

1/3  tsp.  Nature's  Seasons  salt 

1/2  c.  Bisquick 

1  c.  milk 


Put  milk,  Bisquick,  seasoning  salt  and  eggs  in  blender  or  food 
processor,  blending  for  2  minutes.  Mix  cooked  broccoli  with  chicken, 
onion  and  shredded  cheese  (save  some  cheese  for  topping).  Place  in 
quiche  plate;  pour  milk  and  egg  mixture  over  and  put  rest  of  cheese  on 
top.  Bake  at  325°  until  knife  inserted  halfway  between  center  and  edge 
comes  out  clean,  about  35  minutes. 

Ella  H.  Maner

to  taste.

CHICKEN  PIE 

2  or  3  c.  chicken,  cooked  and  1  c.  plain  flour 
chopped                                                    2  tsp.  baking  powder 

1  1/4  c.  chicken  broth  1  tsp.  salt 

1  can  cream  of  celery  soup  or  1/4  tsp.  pepper 

chicken  soup  1  c.  milk 
1  stick  margarine 

In  saucepan  heat  chicken  broth  and  soup  to  boiling.  Add  chicken 
and  set  aside.  In  separate  saucepan  melt  margarine.  Stir  in  drv 
ingredients  (flour,  baking  powder,  salt  and  pepper).  Add  milk  gradual- 
ly, stirring  well  until  slightly  thickened.  Place  chicken  mixture  in  a 
9  x  12-inch  baking  dish.  Pour  flour  mixture  over  chicken  mixture. 
Bake  at  425°  for  30  minutes  or  until  brown.    Makes  6  to  8  servings. 

Joyce  Reid

over    chicken.    Drain    can  of  mixed  vegetables.    Spread  over  margarine.

aside  Mix  1  cup  self-rising  flour  and  1  cup  milk.  Pour  over  vegeta- 
bles. Then  pour  soup  and  broth  over  all.  Cook  at  350"  until  done 
(depending  on  size  of  pan).

BRUNSWICK  STEW 


1  (3  lb.)  fryer 

2  lb.  potatoes 

2  medium  cans  tomatoes 
2  small  cans  butter  beans 
1  small  can  cream-style  corn 
1  (12  oz.)  can  tomato  juice 


1  stick  margarine 

1/4  c.  sugar 

salt  and  pepper  to  taste 

Worcestershire  sauce  to  taste 

Texas  Pete  sauce  to  taste 


Boil  chicken  until  tender.  If  boiled  the  day  before  stew  is  to 
be  prepared,  allow  chicken  to  remain  in  broth  overnight.  Remove 
chicken  from  broth  and  bone.  Cook  potatoes  in  broth,  remove  and  mash. 
Heat  other  vegetables  in  broth,  remove  and  mash.  Place  all  ingredients 
in  an  8  quart  pot.  Simmer  for  1  hour,  stirring  often.  May  be  frozen. 
Makes  7  to  8  quarts. 

Randy  and  Brian  Bowers

CHICKEN  CASSEROLE

cornbread  dressing

chicken

minutes  to  1   hour.

ONE  DISH  HAMBURGER  AND  MACARONI 


1  lb.  ground  beef 
1  large  onion,  sliced 
1  green  pepper,  sliced 

1  c.  short  cut  macaroni, 
uncooked 

2  Tbsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 


1  Tbsp.  parsley 

2  tsp.  oregano 

1  (15  oz.)  can  tomato  sauce 

1  can  water 

2  tsp.  garlic  salt 


Brown  ground  beef  and  drain  off  fat.  Brown  onion  and  pepper. 
Add  macaroni  and  stir  until  it  is  transparent.  Add  tomato  sauce,  water 
and  seasoning.  Cover  and  simmer  20  minutes.  Let  stand  covered  for  5 
minutes  with  heat  off. 

Claudette  Kayler 

ENGLISH  BEEF  POT  PIE 

(For  the  Crock-Pot) 


2  lb.  beef  round  steak,  cut 
into  1-inch  cubes 

3  Tbsp.  flour 

1  tsp.  salt 

1/8  tsp.  pepper 

2  medium  carrots,  pared  and  sliced 


3  medium  potatoes,  peeled  and 

sliced 
1  large  onion,  thinly  sliced 
1  (16  02.)  can  whole  tomatoes 
Biscuit  Topping 


Place  steak  cubes  in  crock-pot.  Combine  flour,  salt  and  pepper 
and  toss  with  steak  to  coat  thoroughly.  Stir  in  remaining  ingredients 
except  Biscuit  Topping  and  mix  thoroughly.  Cover  and  cook  on  low 
setting  for  7  to  10  hours. 

One  hour  before  serving,  remove  meat  and  vegetables  from  crock- 
pot  and  pour  into  shallow  2  1/2  quart  baking  dish.  Preheat  oven  to 
425°.  Cover  meat  mixture  with  Biscuit  Topping.  Bake  for  20  to  25 
minutes.     Yields  4  servings  (about  2  1/2  quarts). 


-24- 


MAIN    DISHES 


Biscuit  Topping: 

2  c.  flour 
1  tsp.  salt 

3  tsp.  baking  powder 


1/4  c.  shortening 
3/4  c.  milk 


Mix  dry  ingredients.  Cut  in  shortening  until  mixture  resembles 
coarse  cornmeal.  Add  milk  all  at  one  time;  stir  well.  Pat  out  on 
floured  board;  roll  out  to  cover  baking  dish. 

Marianne  Bumgarner-Davis 

Ginger  Colson 

ONE  POT  CASSEROLE 


2  lb.  hamburger 

2  medium  onions,  grated 

1  bell  pepper,  finely  chopped 


3  cans  vegetable  soup 

1  c.  catsup 

salt  and  pepper  to  taste 


Saute  hamburger  with  chopped  onions  and  pepper  until  meat  loses 
its  red  color  and  becomes  crumbly.  Drain  off  any  fat  that  accumulates. 
Add  soup,  catsup,  salt  and  pepper.  Put  in  2-quart  casserole.  Bake  at 
375°  about  15  or  20  minutes.  Before  serving,  sprinkle  top  of  casserole 
with  paprika,  parsley  or  cheese. 

Susie  Bowers 

CASHEW  NUT  BEEF  CASSEROLE 


1  lb.  noodles 

3  large  onions,  chopped 

2  lb.  ground  beef 

2  cans  mushroom  soup 
1  large  can  evaporated  milk 


2  (3  oz.)  cans  chow  mein 

noodles 
1  lb.  sharp  cheese,  grated 
1  can  cashew  nuts 


Cook  noodles;  saute  beef  and  onions,  stirring  until  done.  Heat 
soup  and  milk  together  and  add  to  beef  mixture.  Place  layer  of  noodles 
and  layer  of  beef  mixture  in  large  casserole  dish.  Sprinkle  layer  of 
cheese  on  top.  Bake  20  minutes  at  350°.  Top  with  chow  mein  noodles 
and  nuts.     Place  under  broiler  for  a  few  minutes.     Watch  closely.

SWEET  AND  SOUR  MEAT  LOAF 


Sauce: 

1  (18  oz.)  can  tomato  sauce 
1  Tbsp.  mustard 
1/4  c.  vinegar 


1/4  c.  brown  sugar 

1  tsp.  Worcestershire  sauce

-25- 


MAIN    DISHES 


Meat: 

2  lb.  hamburger  1  Tbsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 

1  pkg.  Zesta  crackers,  1  medium  onion 
crumbled  1  tsp.  salt 

2  eggs  pepper  to  taste 

Mix  sauce  ingredients  and  set  aside. 

Mix  together  meat  mixture.  Add  1/2  of  sauce  mix.  Cook  45 
minutes  at  375°.  Drain  grease.  Pour  remaining  sauce  over  meat  loaf 
and  bake  15  minutes.

MEAT  LOAF 

2  lb.  ground  beef  1  can  tomato  soup 

2  small  eggs  2  Tbsp.  each  brown  sugar, 

1  pkg.  Lipton  onion  soup  mix  mustard  and  vinegar 

1  c.  oatmeal  1/2  c.  water 

Mix  meat,  eggs,  soup  mix  and  1/2  can  of  soup.  Make  into  two 
loaves.  Mix  rest  of  tomato  soup,  sugar,  mustard,  vinegar  and  water  in 
jar.  Pour  over  loaves  in  baking  pan.  Baste  occasionally.  Bake  at 
350°  for  1   1/2  hours. 

Virginia  Lee 

HAMBURGER  CASSEROLE 

2  c.  uncooked  noodles  1  c.  grated  sharp  Cheddar 
(heaping)  cheese 

1  lb.  ground  steak  2  tsp.  margarine 

1  can  tomato  sauce  2  c.  water 

1  can  corn  1  small  onion 

1  can  pitted  black  olives 

Brown  ground  steak  and  onion  in  butter  until  red  is  out  of  meat. 
Add  meat,  tomato  sauce  and  1  cup  of  water.  Add  noodles,  stir  and  cook 
until  tender.  Add  more  water  as  necessary.  Salt  and  pepper  to  taste. 
Add  corn  and  olives.  Pour  into  lightly  greased  casserole  dish.  Top 
with  grated  cheese.     Bake  45  minutes  at  350°.

LASAGNE

1  (15  1/2  oz.)  can  tomato 
sauce 


1  c.  cottage  cheese 

6  oz.  Mozzarella  cheese 

1  small  can  mushrooms,  drained 

1  lb.  hamburger 


Cook  noodles  6  minutes  and  drain.  Brown  hamburger  meat.  Add 
oregano  and  tomato  sauce  along  with  the  mushrooms.  In  baking  dish

HAMBURGER  PIE 


1  lb.  ground  beef 
1  c.  chopped  onion 
1  to  2  Tbsp.  chili  powder 
(optional) 


1  can  cream  of  mushroom  soup, 

undiluted 
1  unbaked  9-inch  pastry  shell 
1/2  c.  shredded  Cheddar  cheese 
1  1/2  c.  hot  mashed  potatoes 


Combine  ground  beef  and  onions  in  a  large  skillet;  cook  until 
meat  is  browned  and  onion  is  tender,  stirring  to  crumble  beef.  Drain 
off  drippings.  Stir  in  chili  powder  and  soup;  spoon  into  pastry  shell. 
Bake  at  400°  for  25  minutes.  Remove  from  oven;  sprinkle  with  cheese 
and  spoon  mashed  potatoes  around  inside  edge  of  crust.  Yield:  one 
(9-inch)  pie. 

Kathrene  Collins

CRITTENTON  CASSEROLE 

1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  medium-wide  egg  1/2  c.  chopped  onions 

noodles  salt  and  pepper  to  taste 

1  can  cream  of  mushroom  soup  2  lb.  lean  ground  beef 

1  soup  can  milk  or  more  1  can  Chinese  noodles 

1/2  lb.  grated  sharp  cheese  1/4  lb.  slivered  blanched 
3/4  c.  ripe  olives,  chopped  almonds 

3  Tbsp.  parsley,  chopped  or  parsley  flakes 

Cook  noodles  according  to  package  directions,  drain.  Brown  meat 
lightly  in  heavy  skillet;  add  onions,  salt  and  pepper  and  blend  well. 
Combine  soup  and  milk.  Blend  well.  In  one  large  (or  two  smaller)  not 
too  deep  casserole  put  layers  of  noodles,  cheese,  olives,  parsley  and 
meat.  Repeat  layers  until  all  ingredients  are  used.  Pour  soup  mixture 
over  all,  cover  and  bake  in  350°  oven  for  35  to  40  minutes.  Remove  I 
cover,  top  with  Chinese  noodles  and  almonds.    Bake  for  5  to  10  minutes. 

Note:  If  casserole  seems  too  dry  during  baking,  add  some  more  I 
milk.  May  be  prepared  a  day  ahead  and  refrigerated.  Do  not  add  ] 
noodles  and  nuts  until  after  first  baking. 

This  recipe  from  Eudora  Garrison  in  the  Charlotte  Observer  many 
years  ago. 

Jo  Avert 

BEEF  AND  POTATO  LOAF  | 

1  lb.  lean  ground  beef  1/8  tsp.  pepper 

3/4  c.  evaporated  milk  4  c.  thinly  sliced,  peeled  raw 

1/2  c.  fine  saltine  cracker  potatoes 

crumbs  1  Tbsp.  chopped  onion 

1/4  c.  catsup  salt  and  pepper 

1/4  c.  chopped  onion  1  tsp.  parsley  flakes 
1  tsp.  salt 

Arrange  evenly  in  greased  2-quart  baking  dish  the  potatoes, 
chopped  onion,  salt,  pepper  and  parsley  flakes. 

Mix  ground  beef,  milk,  cracker  crumbs,  catsup,  onion,  salt  and 
pepper.  Spread  evenly  over  potatoes.  Decorate  top  with  more  catsup, 
if  desired.     Bake  in  350°  oven  1  hour  until  potatoes  are  tender.

OVEN  PORCUPINES 


1  lb.  ground  beef 
1/2  c.  uncooked  rice 
1  1/2  c.  water 
1/3  c.  chopped  onion 
1  tsp.  salt 


1/2  tsp.  celery  salt 
1/8  tsp.  garlic  powder 
1/8  tsp.  pepper 

1  (15  oz.)  can  tomato  sauce 

2  tsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 


Heat  oven  to  350°.  Mix  meat,  rice,  1/2  cup  water,  onion,  salts, 
garlic  powder  and  pepper.  Shape  mixture  by  rounded  teaspoonfuls  into 
balls.  Place  meatbails  in  ungreased  baking  dish,  8  x  8  x  2-inches. 
Stir  together  remaining  ingredients,  pour  over  meatballs.  Cover  with 
foil;  bake  45  minutes.     Uncover;  bake  15  minutes  longer.

CORNED  BEEF  SPECIAL 


1  (3  oz.)  pkg.  lemon  gelatin 
1  c.  boiling  water 
1  c.  mayonnaise 
1/2  c.  celery,  chopped  fine 
1/2  c.  bell  pepper,  chopped 
fine 


1/4  to  1/2  c.  onion,  chopped 

fine 
1  (8  1/2  oz.)  can  tiny  green 

peas,  drained 
1  (12  oz.)  can  corned  beef, 

cut  into  small  pieces 


This  can  be  used  as  a  meat  and  vegetable  spread  to  serve  on 
crackers. 

Method:  Dissolve  gelatin  in  boiling  water.  Cool.  Add  mayon- 
naise, then  celery,  bell  pepper,  onion,  peas  and  corned  beef.  Spray  or 
oil  a  six-cup  mold.  Fill  with  mixture  and  chill  until  set.  Unmold  and 
serve. 

Margaret  Lisenby 

BARBECUE  BEEF  CUPS 


1  can  canned  biscuits  (10 

biscuit  size) 
1  lb.  ground  beef 
1/2  c.  pecans 
1/2  c.  catsup 


2  or  2  1/2  tsp.  Worcestershire 

sauce 
4  Tbsp.  lemon  juice 
grated  cheese 


Note:  Can  use  1/2  to  3/4  cup  bottled  barbecue  sauce  instead  of 
catsup,  Worcestershire  sauce  and  lemon  juice. 

Brown  ground  beef  and  pecans.  Use  a  little  oil  if  necessary. 
Drain  grease  thoroughly.  Add  catsup,  Worcestershire  sauce  and  lemon 
juice,  or  if  using  bottled  sauce,  add  it  to  the  beef.  Mix  thoroughly 
and  allow    to    simmer    a    few    minutes  until  flavors  are  mixed. 

Grease  muffin  tin.  Line  each  cup  with  a  biscuit,  pressing  up 
sides  to  form  cups  out  of  the  dough.  Fill  cups  with  beef  mixture. 
Sprinkle  cheese  on  top.    Bake  at  400°  for  15  to  20  minutes. 

Elisabeth  Penry 

FRIED  RICE  WITH  BEEF  AND  ONIONS 


6  c.  cold  cooked  rice 

1  lb.  cooked  beef,  cut  in  thin 

strips 
3  Tbsp.  oil  (for  frying) 


1  large  onion,  cut  lengthwise 
as  thin  as  possible 

2  Tbsp.  cold  water  (to  loosen 
rice) 


-30- 


MAIN    DISHES 


Sauce: 

3  Tbsp.  soy  sauce 
1  Tbsp.  dry  sherry 
1/3  tsp.  salt 


1/8  tsp.  pepper 
1  Tbsp.  cornstarch 


Add  2  tablespoons  cold  water  to  rice.  Loosen  and  separate  the 
grains.  Marinate  beef  in  sauce  for  4  minutes.  Heat  frying  pan  until 
it  is  very  hot,  375°.  Add  oil  and  heat  thoroughly.  Fry  onions  to  a 
light  golden  brown.  Add  beef  with  sauce  and  cook  for  2  to  3  minutes, 
stirring  constantly.  Add  rice  and  mix  with  other  ingredients.  Heat 
thoroughly. 

Gay  Hanback

QUICK  AND  EASY  SHRIMP  CREOLE 


2  Tbsp.  butter 

2  Tbsp.  vegetable  oil 
1/2  c.  chopped  onion 

1/2  c.  chopped  green  pepper 
1/2  c.  chopped  celery 

3  1/2  Tbsp.  flour 
1/3  c.  water 


2  tsp.  sugar 

dash  of  salt,  Tabasco  sauce 

and  chili  powder 
1  large  can  tomatoes 
1  bay  leaf 
parsley 
1  lb.  cooked  shrimp 


63786 


-31- 


MAIN    DISHES 


In  large  skillet,  saute  onion,  pepper  and  celery  in  butter  and 
oil.  Mix  together  the  flour,  water  and  sugar.  Pour  into  skillet, 
mixing  well  and  adding  more  water  if  necessary.  Cut  up  tomatoes  and 
add  to  skillet.  Add  bay  leaf,  salt,  Tabasco  sauce  and  chili  powder  and 
sprinkle  with  parsley.  Simmer  for  20  minutes,  add  shrimp  and  heat  for

SHRIMP  CHOW  MEIN 

1/4  c.  butter  or  oleo  1  tsp.  salt 

1  medium  onion,  chopped  dash  of  pepper 

1  lb.  cooked  and  shelled  1  1/2  c.  hot  water 
shrimp  1  can  mixed  Chinese 

2  c.  chopped  celery  vegetables,  drained 

Thickening: 

2  Tbsp.  cold  water  1  Tbsp.  soy  sauce 

2  Tbsp.  cornstarch  1  tsp.  sugar 

Melt  butter  or  oleo  in  skillet.  Add  onions  and  cook  3  minutes. 
Add  celery,  salt,  pepper  and  hot  water.  Cook  for  10  minutes.  Add 
Chinese  vegetables  and  shrimp.    Cook  5  minutes. 

Dissolve  cornstarch  in  cold  water.  Combine  thickening  ingredi- 
ents and  add  to  mixture.  Cook  2  minutes.  Serve  over  cooked  rice  or 
Chinese  noodles.     Serves  6. 

Bob  Sims 

IMPERIAL  CRAB  CASSEROLE 

1  lb.  crabmeat  1/2  c.  milk 

2  Tbsp.  chopped  onion  1/2  tsp.  salt 

2  Tbsp.  chopped  green  pepper  dash  of  pepper 

3  Tbsp.  oleo,  melted  1/2  tsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 
2  Tbsp.  flour                                              2  hard-boiled  eggs,  chopped 

Remove  any  shell  or  cartilage  from  crabmeat.  Cook  onions  and 
green  pepper  in  the  oleo  until  tender.  Blend  in  flour  gradually.  Add 
milk  slowly  and  cook  until  thick,  stirring  constantly.  Add  seasonings, 
eggs  and  crabmeat.  Place  in  well-greased  casserole.  Buttered  crumbs 
can  be  added.  Bake  in  350°  oven  20  to  25  minutes  until  brown  on  top. 
Serves  4. 

Bob  Sims

OYSTER  PIE 


36  saltine  crackers 
36  oysters,  drained 
3  Tbsp.  butter 


black  pepper 
2  c.  milk 


Break  12  crackers  in  fourths.  Layer  in  dish.  Arrange  1/2  the 
oysters  on  top.  Repeat  layering.  Dot  with  1  tablespoon  butter, 
sprinkle  with  pepper.  Pour  milk  all  over.  Bake  in  400°  oven  15  to  20 
minutes,  until  brown,  not  dry.

STUFFED  PORK  CHOPS  FOR  THE  CROCK-POT 


4  double  pork  loin  chops,  well 

trimmed 
salt  and  pepper  to  taste 
1  (12  oz.)  can  whole  kernel 

corn,  drained 
1  small  onion,  chopped 
1  green  pepper,  seeded  and  chopped 


1  c.  fresh  bread  crumbs 
1/2  tsp.  leaf  oregano  or  leaf 

sage 
1/3  c.  raw  long-grained 

converted  rice 
1  (8  oz.)  can  tomato  sauce 


Cut  a  pocket  in  each  chop,  cutting  from  the  edge  almost  to  the 
bone.  Lightly  season  pockets  with  salt  and  pepper.  In  bowl  combine 
all  ingredients  except  pork  chops  and  tomato  sauce.  Stuff  pork  chops. 
Secure  along  fat  side  with  wooden  picks. 

Pour  any  remaining  vegetable  mixture  into  crock-pot.  Moisten 
top  surface  of  each  chop  with  tomato  sauce.  Add  stuffed  pork  chops  to 
crock-pot,  stacking  to  fit  if  necessary.  Pour  any  remaining  tomato 
sauce  on  top.  Cover  and  cook  on  low  setting  for  7  to  10  hours  or  until 
done.    To  serve,  remove  chops    to    heatproof    platter  and  mound  vegeta-

MAIN    DISHES 


ble-rice  mixture  in  center.     Yield:     4  servings. 

Marianne  Bumgarner-Davis 
Ginger  Colson 

PORK  CHOP  CASSEROLE 

6  medium  potatoes,  thin  sliced  2  tsp.  salt 

3  Tbsp.  butter  1/2  tsp.  pepper 

6  pork  chops  1  1/2  c.  milk 

Arrange  potatoes  in  greased  pan,  dot  with  butter.  Arrange  chops 
over  potatoes,  sprinkle  with  salt  and  pepper.  Pour  milk  over  chops  and 
potatoes.    Bake  at  350°  for  45  minutes  or  until  chops  are  golden  brown. 

Linda  A.  Henry 

TOURTERE  DE  NOEL 

(Pork  Pie) 


2  c.  sifted  all-purpose  flour 

1/2  tsp.  salt 

1/2  c.  butter  or  oleo 

1  egg,  lightly  beaten 

2  Tbsp.  cold  water 

2  Tbsp.  butter  or  oleo 

1  1/2  lb.  lean  pork,  finely 
chopped 

2  c.  chopped  onion  (2  large) 


1  clove  garlic,  minced 

1/2  tsp.  celery  seed 

1  (10  3/4  oz.)  can  condensed 

chicken  broth 
1/2  tsp.  salt 
1/4  tsp.  pepper 
1/4  tsp.  ground  sage 
1  egg  yolk 
1  Tbsp.  water 


Sift  flour  and  salt.  Cut  in  butter  until  mixture  resembles 
cornmeal.  Add  egg  and  3  tablespoons  water;  stir  with  fork  until  all 
particles  are  moistened  and  pastry  clings  together;  shape  into  a  ball. 
Wrap  in  plastic  wrap  and  refrigerate  one  to  two  hours.  Heat  butter  in 
large  skillet  over  medium  heat.  Add  chopped  pork.  Cook,  stirring 
until  meat  loses  its  red  color.  Add  onion  and  garlic;  cook  2  minutes, 
stirring  occasionally.  Add  celery  seed,  chicken  broth,  salt,  pepper 
and  sage.  Cover  skillet.  Bring  to  a  boil;  lower  heat.  Simmer  35  to 
40  minutes  or  until  all  liquid  has  evaporated,  stirring  occasionally. 
Remove  skillet  from  heat;     set  aside  to  cool. 

Heat  oven  to  450°.  Divide  dough  in  half.  Roll  1/2  out  and 
place  in  9  or  10-inch  greased  pie  plate.  Spoon  in  filling  and  cover 
with  other  half  of  dough.  Cut  vent  in  center  of  top  crust.  Beat  egg 
yolk  and  1  tablespoon  water  just  until  blended.  Brush  over  top  of  pie. 
Bake  10  minutes.    Reduce  heat  to    350°.    Bake  25  minutes  or  until  crust 

is  brown.     Serves  6  to  8. 

Margaret  Lisenby

SPICY  PORK  AND  CABBAGE  FOR  THE  CROCK-POT 


4  to  6  pork  loin  chops  (about 
1-inch  thick,  well  trimmed) 

salt  and  pepper  to  taste 

Kitchen  Bouquet 

4  c.  coarsely  shredded  cabbage 

3  to  4  tart  apples,  cored  and 
diced 


1/2  small  onion,  chopped 
2  whole  cloves 
1/2  small  bay  leaf 
1/4  c.  sugar 

1  c.  water 

2  Tbsp.  cider  vinegar 
2  tsp.  salt 


Season  pork  chops  lightly  with  salt  and  pepper  and  brush  with 
Kitchen  Bouquet;  set  aside.  Place  cabbage,  apples  and  onions  in 
crock-pot.  Add  remaining  ingredients,  except  pork  chops.  Toss  togeth- 
er well  to  distribute  evenly  the  spices.  Arrange  chops  on  top  of 
cabbage  mixture,  stacking  to  fit.  Cover  and  cook  on  low  setting  for  7 
to  10  hours.     (On  high  setting  for     2     to     3     hours.)     Yield:     4     to     6 

servings. 

Marianne  Bumgarner-Davis

MEATS,  POULTRY  &  SEAFOOD 


ORIENTAL  ROAST  PORK 


4  to  7  lb.  pork  loin 

1  Tbsp.  flour 

1/4  c.  lemon  juice 
1/4  c.  soy  sauce 

2  Tbsp.  catsup 


1  clove  garlic,  minced 

1/2  tsp.  salt 

1  Tbsp.  sugar 

1/2  tsp.  ground  ginger 


Shake  1  tablespoon  flour  in  empty  Brown-in-Bag  and  place  in  pan. 
Trim  excess  fat  to  a  thin  layer.  Place  pork  loin  in  bag.  Combine 
remaining  ingredients  and  pour  into  bag.  Close  bag  with  twist  tie  and 
gently  turn  several  times  to  coat  pork.  Refrigerate  3  to  4  hours  or 
overnight.  Preheat  oven  to  350°.  Remove  roast  from  refrigerator. 
Follow  Brown-in-Bag  cooking  instructions.  Cook  for  2  1/2  to  3  1/2 
hours  or  until  meat  thermometer  reads  170°. 

Pat  Reid 


BEEF  TIPS  ON  RICE 


3  Tbsp.  plain  flour 

1  tsp.  salt 

1/2  tsp.  pepper 
1/2  tsp.  paprika 

2  lb.  boneless  sirloin  top 
roast,  cut  into  1-inch 
cubes 


2  Tbsp.  vegetable  oil 
2  large  onions,  sliced  or 

chopped 
1  beef  bouillon  cube 
3/4  c.  boiling  water 
hot  cooked  rice 


Combine  flour,  salt,  pepper  and  paprika  in  a  plastic  bag;  shake 
to  mix.  Place  beef  cubes  in  bag  and  shake  well.  Heat  oil  in  a  Dutch 
oven;  add  beef  and  cook  until  browned.  Add  onions;  cook  until  tender. 
Dissolve  bouillon  cube  in  boiling  water;  add  to  beef  mixture.  Cover, 
reduce  heat  and  simmer  2  hours,  stirring  occasionally.  Serve  over 
rice.     Serves  6  to  8. 

Nita  Bunn 

MARINATED  ROAST 


3  lb.  shoulder  roast  or  eye  of 
round  or  London  broil 

1  tsp.  Accent 

1/3  c.  wine  vinegar 

2  Tbsp.  cooking  oil 
2  Tbsp.  soy  sauce 


1  Tbsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 

1  tsp.  mustard 

1  tsp.  salt 

1/4  tsp.  pepper 

1/4  tsp.  garlic  powder 


Marinate   in  refrigerator  2  to      3     days.      The  day  of  cooking,   set

meat  out  to  warm  up    before    cooking.    Cook    on    grill  approximately  45 
minutes  to  1  hour.    Spoon  marinade  over  meat  while  cooking.

HERBED  BEEF  KABOBS 


1/4  c.  salad  oil 

2  Tbsp.  vinegar 

1  tsp.  onion  salt 

1  tsp.  celery  salt 

3/4  tsp.  garlic  salt  or  garlic 

granulated 
1  tsp.  oregano 


1/2  tsp.  pepper 

1  Tbsp.  prepared  mustard 

1  small  bay  leaf 

2  lb.  boneless  sirloin 
green  pepper  squares 
fresh  mushrooms 


Combine  all  ingredients  except  meat,  green  pepper  and  mushrooms 
in  a  saucepan.  Heat  to  boiling  point  and  cool.  Cut  meat  into  1-inch 
squares.  Add  to  mixture.  Mix  well  and  marinate  for  1  to  2  days.  Add 
mushrooms  and  green  peppers  to  skewers  when  cooking  on  grill. 

Carolyn  Trail 

SWISS  STEAK  WITH  MOZZARELLA 


2  lb.  beef  round  steak 
1/2-inch  thick 

3  Tbsp.  plain  flour 

1  (1  lb.)  can  tomatoes 
1/4  tsp.  basil  leaves 
1/2  c.  chopped  onion 


1  1/2  c.  (6  oz.)  shredded 

Mozzarella  cheese 
1/4  c.  (1/2  stick)  margarine 
1  1/2  tsp.  salt 
1/8  tsp.  pepper 
1/2  c.  chopped  green  pepper 


Cut  meat  into  serving  pieces;  coat  with  flour.  Melt  margarine 
in  heavy  pan  with  lid.  Brown  meat  slowly  on  all  sides.  Add  tomatoes, 
salt,  basil  and  pepper.  Cover  and  simmer  for  1  hour.  Add  onion  and 
green  pepper.  Cook  25  to  30  minutes  more.  Add  some  water  if  meat 
becomes  too  dry.  Pour  into  heatproof  serving  dish;  top  meat  with 
cheese.  Heat  in  oven  until  cheese  melts.  Serve  over  rice.  Yield:  8 
servings. 

Gail  T.  Bunn 


CHICKEN  BITES 


4  large  skinned  and  boned 

chicken  breast  halves 
1  whole  egg 


2  Tbsp.  vegetable  oil 

2  Tbsp.  soy  sauce 

1/2  c.  buttermilk  baking  mix 


Preheat  oven  to  450°.  Generously  spray  cookie  sheet  with 
nonstick  spray.  Beat  together  egg,  oil  and  soy  sauce.  Mix  in  baking 
mix  to  form  a  batter.  Cut  chicken  into  1-inch  bite-size  pieces. 
Thoroughly  coat  chicken  with  batter.  Place  in  single  layer  on  cookie 
sheet  so  that  pieces  do  not  touch.  Bake  approximately  12  to  15  minutes 
until  golden  brown  and  tender.     Serves  4. 

Elisabeth  Penry

BAKED  CHICKEN  SOUFFLE 


8  slices  bread  with  crust 

removed  (French) 
6  c.  cooked  chicken,  cubed 
8  to  10  oz.  mushrooms  sauteed 

in  1/4  c.  butter 
1  oz.  water  chestnuts,  sliced 
1/2  c.  mayonnaise 


8  slices  sharp  American  cheese 
4  eggs,  well  beaten  with  mixer 
2  c.  milk 
2  cans  cream  of  mushroom  soup, 

undiluted 
1  tsp.  salt 
1  (2  oz.)  jar  chopped  pimentos 


Layer  bread  in  bottom  of  greased  pan.  Spoon  on  chicken.  Pour 
over  the  mushrooms  and  butter.  Layer  water  chestnuts.  Dot  on  mayon- 
naise. Layer  cheese.  Mix  eggs,  milk  and  salt.  Pour  over  all.  Mix 
pimentos  with  mushroom  soup  and  spread  over  all.  Cover  and  let  stand 
overnight  in  refrigerator.  Bake  1  hour  covered  at  350°.  Let  stand 
about  10  minutes  before  slicing  to  serve. 

Sarah  Lee 

SWEET  AND  SOUR  CHICKEN 


1  lb.  cooked  chicken,  cubed 
1  1/4  c.  chicken  broth 

(bouillon  cubes  are  fine) 
1/4  c.  soy  sauce 
3  Tbsp.  vinegar 
3  Tbsp.  brown  sugar 


1/2  tsp.  ginger 

1  can  pineapple  chunks  and 

juice 
1  c.  carrot  strips 
1  c.  green  pepper  strips 
1  Tbsp.  cornstarch 


Mix  broth,  soy  sauce,  vinegar  and  pineapple  juice  in  saucepan. 
Add  carrot  strips  and  cook  until  barely  tender.  Add  chicken,  pineap- 
ple, brown  sugar  and  ginger.  Cook  20  minutes.  Add  green  pepper  strips 
and  cook  about  5  minutes.  Thicken  with  cornstarch.  Serve  over  rice, 
noodles  or  toast. 

Evelyn  Norwood 

JADE  TREE  CHICKEN

boned  and  skinned

and  sliced)

salt  and  red  pepper  blending  well.  Add  chicken  and  turn  to  coat. 
Cover  and  marinate  in  refrigerator  for  20  minutes.  Place  remaining  oil 
in  large  skillet  and     heat     to     medium-high  temperature.     Add  broccoli,

celery  and  onion.  Stir-fry  for  6  minutes  or  until  crisp-tender. 
Remove  vegetables  and  set  aside.  In  same  skillet  stir-fry  chicken  for 
5  minutes  or  until  opaque  and  fork  tender.  Return  vegetables  to  pan.

FIX  NOW  BAKE  LATER  CHICKEN 


4  chicken  breasts,  split 
8  slices  bacon 
1  (2  1/2  oz.)  jar  dried  beef, 
shredded 


1  (10  3/4  oz.)  can  cream  of 

mushroom  soup 
1  c.  sour  cream

BARBECUED  CHICKEN 


3  lb.  or  less  chicken,  cut  up 
1  medium  onion,  chopped 
1  c.  catsup 
1  c.  water 


2  Tbsp.  Worcestershire  sauce 
2  Tbsp.  brown  sugar 
2  Tbsp.  vinegar 
2  Tbsp.  mustard 


Mix  catsup,  water,  Worcestershire  sauce,  brown  sugar,  vinegar 
and  mustard.  Brown  chicken  slowly  in  1/4  cup  oil  (as  for  frying).

and  simmer  10  minutes.  Put  chicken  back  in  pan.  Cook  until  done  or 
place  in  baking  dish  and    pour    sauce    over.    Bake    in    325°  oven  until 

done. 

Ruby  Barbee

How  To  Can  Vegetables 


POINTS  ON  PACKING 

Raw  pack.  -  Pack  cold  raw  vegetables 
(except  corn,  lima  beans,  and  peas) 
tightly  into  container  and  cover  with 
boiling  water. 

Hot  pack.  -  Preheat  vegetables  in  water 
or  steam.  Cover  with  cooking  liquid  or 
boiling  water.  Cooking  liquid  is  recom- 
mended for  packing  most  vegetables 
because  it  may  contain  minerals  and 
vitamins  dissolved  out  of  the  food. 
Boiling  water  is  recommended  when 
cooking  liquid  is  dark,  gritty,  or  strong- 
flavored,  and  when  there  isn't  enough 
cooking  liquid. 

PROCESSING  IN  A  PRESSURE  CANNER 

Use  a  steam-pressure  canner  for 
processing  all  vegetables  except  toma- 
toes and  pickled  vegetables. 

Directions.  -  Follow  the  manufacturer's 
directions  for  the  canner  you  are  using. 
Here  are  a  few  pointers  on  the  use  of  any 
steam-pressure  canner: 

•Put  2  or  3  inches  of  boiling  water  in 
the  bottom  of  the  canner;  the  amount  of 
water  to  use  depends  on  the  size  and 
shape  of  the  canner. 

•Set  filled  glass  jars  or  tin  cans  on  rack 
in  canner  so  that  steam  can  flow  around 
each  container.    If  two  layers  of  cans  or 
jars  are  put  in,  stagger  the  second  layer. 
Use  a  rack  between  layers  of  glass  jars. 

•Fasten  canner  cover  securely  so  that 
no  steam  can  escape  except  through  vent 
(petcock  or  weighted-gage  opening) . 

•Watch  until  steam  pours  steadily  from 
vent.  Let  it  escape  for  10  minutes  or  more 
to  drive  all  air  from  the  canner.  Then 
close  petcock  or  put  on  weighted  gage. 

•Let  pressure  rise  to  10  pounds  (240 
degrees  F.)  The  moment  this  pressure  is 
reached  start  counting  processing  time. 
Keep  pressure  constant  by  regulating 
heat  under  the  canner.  Do  not  lower 
pressure  by  opening  petcock.  Keep 
drafts  from  blowing  on  canner. 

•When  processing  time  is  up,  remove 
canner  from  heat  immediately. 

With  glass  jars,  let  canner  stand  until 
pressure  is  zero.  Never  try  to  rush  the 
cooling  by  pouring  cold  water  over  the 
canner.  When  pressure  registers  zero, 
wait  a  minute  or  two,  then  slowly  open 


petcock  or  take  off  weighted  gage. 
Unfasten  cover  and  tilt  the  far  side  up  so 
steam  escapes  away  from  you.   Take  jars 
from  canner. 

HOW  TO  CHECK  CANNING  JARS 

The  first  step  in  home  canning  should 
take  place  long  before  food  and  equip- 
ment are  assembled  and  ready  to  go. 
Jars  and  other  supplies  should  be 
checked  prior  to  the  canning  session.  In 
that  way,  you  can  replace  damaged 
supplies  and  purchase  new  ones  to  avoid 
costly  delays  or  inconvenience. 

Here  are  some  tips  to  help  you. 

Choosing  mason  jars.  Jars  manufac- 
tured especially  for  home  canning  generi- 
cally  are  called  mason  jars  and  must  be 
used  when  preserving.  They  are  designed 
with  a  specially  threaded  mouth  for 
proper  sealing  with  mason  lids.  So,  can 
with  standard  mason  jars  only. 

Preparing  glass  Jars.  Check  all  jars, 
rings,  and  lids  carefully.  Discard  any 
with  nicks  or  cracks  in  top  sealing  edge 
and  threads  that  may  prevent  airtight 
seals.  Rings  should  be  free  of  dents  or 
rust.  Select  the  size  of  closures  - 
widemouth  or  regular  -  that  fits  your  jar. 
Wash  jars  in  hot,  soapy  water  and  rinse 
well.  Then  place  in  boiling  water  for 
10-15  minutes.  Keep  jars  in  hot  water 
until  ready  to  use.  Boil  lids  according  to 
package  directions. 

Closing  glass  Jars.  Always  wipe  jar  rim 
clean  after  food  product  is  packed.  Place 
lid  on  jar  with  button  side  up.  Screw 
rings  on  firmly,  but  don't  force.  Do  not 
re-tighten  rings  after  processing  or 
cooling. 

A  new  lid  that  snaps  down  and  clicks  as 
the  jar  cools,  providing  visible  proof  of 
sealing,  called  Magic  Button  (R)  is  made 
by  Owens-Illinois.  Its  read  button  pops 
up  when  the  seal  is  broken.  The  Magic 
Mason  jars  that  go  with  the  special  lids 
have  metric  measurements  as  well  as 
customary  U.S.  measurements  molded  on 
the  side. 

Jar  transfer.  Use  jar  lifter  or  long- 
handled  canning  tongs  to  transfer  jars  to 
and  from  canner  safely.  Place  hot  jars  on 
rack  or  towel,  allowing  2 -inches  of  air 
space  on  all  sides  for  jars  to  cool  evenly.

VEGETABLES 


FRIED  GREEN  ONIONS 

1/2  c.  hot  water 
1  Tbsp.  sugar 


Chop  green  onions  and  tops  coarsely.  Pour  one  tablespoon  of 
grease  in  iron  skillet.  Heat  and  then  place  in  enough  onions  to  fill 
pan.  Add  1/2  cup  of  water.  Cook  slowly  for  about  30  minutes.  Just 
before  it  is  done,  sprinkle  one  tablespoon  of  sugar  over  onions  and 
salt  to  taste.     DO  NOT  stir  while  cooking.     Serve  while  hot. 

Roy  Skidmore 

ONION  CASSEROLE 


4  or  5  medium  onions 

1/2  stick  butter  or  margarine 

salt 

pepper 


1  can  golden  mushroom  soup 
1  c.  grated  sharp  cheese 
crushed  potato  chips 


Slice  onions  and  boil  in  water  until  tender.  Drain.  Add 
margarine,  salt  and  pepper  to  taste  and  soup.  Top  with  cheese  and  bake 
at  350°  until  bubbly,  about  30  minutes.  Remove  from  oven  and  top  with 
potato  chips.     Bake  5  more  minutes. 

Cindy  Beane

MARINATED  CARROTS 


carrots 

1  medium  onion 

1  small  green  pepper 

1  can  tomato  soup 

1/2  c.  salad  oil 

3/4  c.  vinegar 


1  tsp.  prepared  mustard

NANNY'S  CANDIED  YAMS 


4  to  5  large  sweet  potatoes 
1  c.  granulated  sugar 
1  to  2  c.  butter 


3  to  4  c.  water 
1  to  2  tsp.  nutmeg 
1  to  2  tsp.  salt 


Select  yellow  yams.  Wash  and  peel.  Cut  them  lengthwise  in  1  to 
4-inch  slices.  Place  in  baking  pan.  Cover  with  3  to  4  cups  water  and 
boil  until  tender  but  not  soft.  Sprinkle  slices  with  sugar,  salt  and 
nutmeg.     Dot  with  butter  and  bake  until  syrup  is  formed,  about  15  or  20 

minutes. 

Beth  Bowers

PARTY  POTATOES 


8  to  10  medium  potatoes 
1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese 
1  carton  sour  cream 
4  Tbsp.  butter 


paprika,  salt  and  pepper  to 
taste 

1/3  c.  chopped  chives  (if 
dried  ones  are  used,  soak 
them  in  water  and  drain) 


Peel,  slice  and  boil  potatoes.  While  they're  cooking,  beat  sour 
cream  and  cream  cheese  until  smooth.  Add  hot  (drained)  potatoes, 
butter,  chives,  paprika,  salt  and  pepper  and  beat  until  smooth.  Put  in 
buttered  oblong  casserole.  Right  before  serving,  bake  at  350°  for  25 
minutes.     Serves  10. 

Mary  Ella  Vick

Morton  Nature's  Seasons 
cheese

sprinkle  with  Parmesan  cheese  or  grated  cheese.

GREEN  AND  GOLD  CASSEROLE 


1  medium  onion,  chopped 

1  Tbsp.  butter 

1  (10  oz.)  can  cheese  soup 

1  (6  oz.)  roll  nippy  cheese 
(optional) 

1/2  tsp.  garlic  powder 

2  or  3  c.  hot,  cooked  rice 


1  (3  oz.)  can  French  fried 

onions 
1  jar  mushroom  pieces 
1  (10  oz.)  pkg.  frozen 

broccoli,  cooked  and 

drained 


Cook  onions  in  butter  until  tender  but  not  brown.  Add  soup, 
cheese  and  garlic.  Cook  over  low  heat,  stirring  until  cheese  melts. 
Add  mushrooms  and  the  liquid,  broccoli  and  rice.  Pour  into  shallow 
greased  casserole.  Bake  15  to  20  minutes  until  hot  and  bubbly.  Top 
with  French  fried  onions  the  last  5  minutes  of  baking.  May  prepare  day 
before  and  refrigerate.     Bake  when  ready  to  use.

1  large  can  milk 
salt  and  pepper 


1  to  2  c.  bread  crumbs 
1  stick  margarine 


Set  oven  to  350°.  Wash  and  chop  or  shred  cabbage.  Place  in  12 
x  9  x  3-inch  baking  dish  or  pan.  Pour  in  large  can  of  milk.  Add  salt 
and  pepper.  Use  bread  crumbs.  Put  margarine  on  top.  Cover  dish  with 
foil  and  bake  30  minutes  covered.    Uncover  and  bake  30  minutes  more. 

Ethel  Bialock

VEGETABLES

ZUCCHINI  CASSEROLE

or  yellow  squash

1  egg

1  medium  onion,  chopped 


1  pkg.  Pepperidge  Farm  herbal  dressing 

Melt  margarine  in  9  x  13-inch  casserole  dish.  Place  dressing  in

Baking  Tips 


COMMON  PROBLEMS 
[Common  Failures] 

Biscuits 
Rough  biscuits 
Dry  biscuits 
Uneven  browning 


Breads  (yeast) 
Porous  bread 

Crust  is  dark  and  blisters  just 
under  the  crust 
Bread  does  not  rise 
Bread  is  streaked 
Bread  bakes  unevenly 

Cakes 
Cracks  and  uneven  surface 

Dry  cakes 


Heavy  cakes 
Sticky  crust 
Coarse  grained  cake 


Fallen  cakes 


Uneven  color 


Uneven  browning 
Cookies 
Uneven  browning 


Soggy  Cookies 

Excessive  spreading  of  cookies 

Muffins 
Coarse  texture 

Tunnels  in  muffins,  peaks  in 
center  and  soggy  texture 
Pies 
Pastry  crumbles 
Pastry  tough 

Pies  do  not  brown 
(fruit  or  custard) 


CAUSES  OF  PROBLEMS 
[Causes  of  Failures] 

Insufficient  mixing 

Baking  in  to  slow  an  oven  and  handling  too 

much 

Cooking  in  dark  surface  pan,  too  high  a 

temperature  and  rolling  the  dough  too  thin 

Over-rising   or   cooking   at   too    low    a 
temperature 

Under-rising 

Over-kneading  or  using  old  yeast 

Under-kneading  and  not  kneading  evenly 

Using  old,  dark  pans,  too  much  dough  in 

pan,  crowding  the  oven  shelf  or  cooking  at 

too  high  a  temperature 

Too   much    flour,    too   hot   an   oven    and 

sometimes  from  cold  oven  start 

Too  much  flour,  too  little  shortening  too 

much  baking  powder  or  cooking  at  too  low  a 

temperature 

Too  much  sugar  or  baking  too  short  a  period 

Too  much  sugar 

Too  little  mixing,  too  much  shortening,  too 

much  baking  powder,  using  shortening  too 

soft,  and  baking  at  too  low  a  temperature 

Using  insufficient  flour,  under  baking,  too 

much  sugar,  too  much  shortening  or  not 

enough  baking  powder 

Cooking  at  too  high  a  temperature,  crowding 

the  shelf  (allow  at  least  2  inches  around  pans) 

or  using  dark  pans 

Not  mixing  well 

Not  using  shiny  cookie  sheet  or  not  allowing 

at  least  2  inches  on  all  sides  of  cookie  sheets 

in  oven 

Cooling  cookies  in  pans  instead  of  racks 

Dropping  cookies  onto  hot  cookie  sheets;  not 

chilling  dough;  not  baking  at  correct 

temperature 

Insufficient  stirring  and  cooking  at  too  low  a 

temperature 

Overmixing 


Over-mixing  flour  and  shortening 

Using  too  much  water  and  over-mixing  the 

dough 

Bake  at  constant  temperature  (400-425 

degrees  )  in  Pyrex  or  enamel  pie  pan

CHEESE  PIE 

(10-inch) 

1  graham  cracker  crust  1  tsp.  vanilla 

1/8  tsp.  nutmeg  1/2  c.  sugar 

1  1/2  lb.  cream  cheese  blueberry  or  cherry  pie 

2  Tbsp.  flour  filling 

2  eggs 

Make  graham  cracker  crust  and  add  1/8  teaspoon  nutmeg.  Beat 
cream  cheese,  flour,  eggs,  vanilla  and  sugar  15  minutes.  Put  in  pie 
shell.     Bake  20  minutes  at  350°.     Top  with  pie  filling.     Chill. 

Gay  Hanback 

HOMEMADE  CHOCOLATE  ICE  CREAM  PIE 

1  (14  oz.)  can  Eagle  Brand  2  c.  (1  pt.)  whipping  cream, 
sweetened  condensed  milk  whipped 

(not  evaporated  milk)  2  chocolate  flavored 

2/3  c.  Hershey's  syrup  Ready-Crust  pie  crusts 

In  large  bowl,  stir  together  sweetened  condensed  milk  and  syrup. 
Fold  in  whipped  cream.  Pour  into  2  chocolate-flavored  pie  crusts  or 
make  one  pie  and  freeze  remaining  as  ice  cream.  Freeze  overnight  or 
for  several  hours. 

Linda  Robinson 

KEY  LIME  PIE 

1  can  Eagle  Brand  milk  green  food  coloring 

1  (6  oz.)  can  frozen  limeade  lime  slices 

1  small  container  Cool  Whip  1  pt.  lime  sherbet 
1  graham  cracker  pie  crust 

Combine  milk,  limeade  and  half  of  Cool  Whip.  Fold  with  sherbet, 
add  3  drops  of  green  food  coloring.  Pour  into  crust.  Garnish  with 
remaining  Cool  Whip  and  lime  slices.     Chill  overnight. 

Ora  Mae  Lisk 

ALASKAN  ORANGE  PIE 

3  1/2  c.  Rice  Chex  crushed  to  2  c.  softened  vanilla  ice 
1  c.  cream 

7  Tbsp.  butter,  melted  2  c.  softened  orange  sherbet 

1/3  c.  plus  6  Tbsp.  sugar  3  egg  whites 

1/2  c.  flaked  coconut  1/4  tsp.  cream  of  tartar 

1/2  tsp.  vanilla 

Prepare  pie  plate.     Bake     Chex    crumbs  in  shallow  pan  10  minutes 

63786  _51_ 


BREADS,  ROLLS,  PIES  &  PASTRY 


at  350°.  Combine  with  melted  butter,  sugar  and  coconut.  Mix  well. 
Press  into  bottom  and  sides  of  pie  plate.  Combine  ice  cream  and 
sherbet  in  large  bowl  of  electric  mixer.  Blend  on  low  speed.  Pour 
into  crust.  Place  in  freezer.  Beat  egg  whites  with  vanilla  and  cream 
of  tartar  until  soft  peaks  form.  Gradually  add  6  tablespoons  sugar. 
Beat  until  stiff  peaks  form.  Spread  meringue  over  filling  carefully 
sealing  to  crust.     Freeze  overnight. 

To  serve:     Bake  in  preheated    475°  oven  2  to  2  1/2  minutes  until 
meringue  is  slightly  browned. 

Claudette  Kayler 


HAWAIIAN  PIE 


1  large  carton  Cool  Whip 
1  can  crushed  pineapple 
juice  of  3  lemons 
1  can  Eagle  Brand  milk 


1  c.  chopped  pecans 

1  small  can  coconut  (may  omit) 

1  graham  cracker  pie  crust 


Mix  until  thick,  Cool  Whip,  milk  and  lemon  juice.  Add  other 
ingredients  and  pour  into  a  graham  cracker  pie  crust.  Chill  overnight. 
Makes  1  large  pie. 

Nell  Colson 

HAWAIIAN  PIE 


1  (9  oz.)  container  Cool  Whip 
1  (17  oz.)  can  crushed 

pineapple,  drained 
1  can  sweetened  condensed  milk 
juice  of  2  lemons 
1  small  pkg.  frozen  coconut 


2  large  ripe  bananas 

pecans  or  walnuts 

2  homemade  graham  cracker 

crusts  or  2  baked  pie 

shells 


Stir  drained  pineapple  into  Cool  Whip.  Stir  the  lemon  juice 
into  the  sweetened  condensed  milk.  Stir  coconut  and  lemon  juice 
mixture  into  the  Cool  Whip  mixture.  Slice  1  banana  in  each  of  the  pie 
crusts.  Pour  mixture  evenly  into  the  two  crusts.  Sprinkle  coconut  and 
chopped  nuts  on  top.     Refrigerate. 

Note:  Coconut  and  bananas  may  be  omitted  and  the  pie  is  still 
delicious. 

Gail  T.  Bunn

LEMON  CHEESE  TARTS 

(Tiny) 

2  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese  3  eggs,  separated 

3/4  c.  granulated  sugar  1  tsp.  lemon  extract 

Sour  Cream  Topping: 

1  c.  sour  cream  1  tsp.  vanilla 

2  1/2  Tbsp.  sugar 

Stir  together  topping   ingredients   until   well   blended. 

Cream  cheese,  sugar  and  egg  yolks.    Add  lemon  extract.    Beat  the 

3  egg  whites  until  stiff  peaks  form.  Fold  into  cheese  mixture. 
Generously  grease  tiny  muffin  tins  with  Crisco  and  dust  with  about  1 
teaspoon  each  graham  cracker  crumbs.  Fill  tins  half  full  with  cheese 
mixture.  Bake  at  350°  for  15  minutes.  Remove  from  oven  and  cool  5 
minutes.  Top  with  the  sour  cream  mixture,  about  1  teaspoon.  Return  to 
oven  5  minutes  or  until  set.  Cool  10  minutes,  remove  from  pan.  Makes 
about  60  tiny  tarts.     Keep  refrigerated. 

Gail  T.  Bunn 

LEMON  MERINGUE  PIE 

1  1/2  c.  sugar  4  egg  yolks,  slightly  beaten 

1/3  c.  cornstarch  2  Tbsp.  butter  or  margarine 

1/4  tsp.  salt  1/4  c.  lemon  juice 

Meringue: 

2/3  c.  egg  whites  (4)  1/4  tsp.  cream  of  tartar 

1/4  tsp.  salt  2/3  c.  sugar 

In   saucepan,   combine   sugar,    cornstarch   and   salt.      Gradually   stir 


-54- 


BREADS,  ROLLS,  PIES  &  PASTRY 


in  1  1/2  cups  water.  Bring  to  a  boil  over  medium  heat,  stirring 
constantly.  Boil  1  minute.  Mixture  will  be  thick  and  clear.  Remove 
from  heat.  Stir  a  little  hot  mixture  into  egg  yolks.  Mix  well.  Pour 
back  into  saucepan.  Stir  again  and  boil  1  minute.  Remove  from  heat. 
Add  butter  and  stir  until  melted.  Add  lemon  juice.  Pour  into  pie 
shell.  Makes  1  deep-dish  or  2  regular  pies.  Cool  while  making  me- 
ringue. 

Beat  egg  whites  until  foamy.  Add  salt  and  cream  of  tartar. 
Beat  to  blend.  Add  sugar,  1  tablespoon  at  a  time.  Beat  until  stiff. 
Top  pie  and  brown  in  oven. 

Pam  Lisenby 

SOUTHERN  STYLE  RAISIN  PIE 

2  c.  raisins  4  Tbsp.  cornstarch 

1  c.  boiling  water  1  Tbsp.  butter 

1/8  tsp.  salt  1/3  c.  orange  juice 

3/4  c.  sugar  1  tsp.  orange  rind 

2  Tbsp.  lemon  juice  1  pie  crust 

Cook  raisins  in  boiling  water  with  salt,  sugar,  lemon  juice  and 
cornstarch  until  thick.  Add  orange  juice,  rind  and  butter.  Let  cool. 
Put  in  unbaked  pie  shell.  Place  pie  crust  on  top  or  lattice  strips  of 
pastry.  Bake  at  450°  for  10  minutes,  then  turn  oven  back  to  350°  until 
done. 

Ella  H.  Maner 

PEACH  COBBLER 

1/4  c.  shortening  1/4  tsp.  salt 

1/2  c.  sugar  1/4  c.  milk 

1  egg  1/2  tsp.  lemon  juice 

1  1/2  c.  flour  peaches  or  any  other  fruit  you 

2  tsp.  baking  powder  desire 

Sift  dry  ingredients  together.  Cream  butter,  add  sugar.  Add 
egg  and  beat  well.  Alternate  dry  ingredients  with  liquid.  Butter 
casserole.  Sprinkle  dish  with  3  tablespoons  brown  sugar.  Then  place  a 
layer  of  peaches  or  any  other  fruit  desired.  Cover  with  batter  and 
bake  at  400°  for  35  to  40  minutes. 

Sarah  C.  Skidmore 

BEST  PEACH  COBBLER 

8  firm  peaches,  peeled  and  1  tsp.  baking  powder 

sliced  or  one  large  can  1/4  tsp.  salt 

sliced  peaches  1/2  c.  milk 

1  stick  margarine  1/4  tsp.  vanilla 

11 /2  c.  sugar  1/2  c.  water 
1  c.  plain  flour 


63786  .55. 


BREADS,  ROLLS.  PIES  &  PASTRY 


Grease  10-inch  casserole  dish.  Line  with  peaches.  Cream 
margarine  and  1/2  cup  sugar.  Mix  flour,  baking  powder  and  salt  and  add 
to  cream  mixture  alternately  with  milk.  Add  vanilla.  Spoon  mixture 
over  peaches.  Mix  remaining  sugar  with  1/2  cup  of  water  or  use  the 
peach  juice  if  using  canned  peaches.  Bring  to  a  boil  and  stir  until 
sugar  dissolves.  Pour  over  batter.  Bake  at  350°  for  1  hour  or  until 
top  browns.

SOUTHERN  STRAWBERRY  PIE 

3/4  c.  sugar  1  Tbsp.  strawberry  flavored 
2  Tbsp.  cornstarch  gelatin 

2  Tbsp.  light  corn  syrup  1  qt  fresh  strawberries 

1  c.  sugar  1  (9-inch)  baked  pie  shell 

Combine  sugar,  cornstarch,  corn  syrup  and  water  in  a  saucepan. 
Bring  to  a  boil.  Cook,  stirring  constantly  until  clear  and  thickened. 
Add  gelatin,  stirring  until  dissolved.  Cool.  Place  strawberries  in 
pie  shell,  pour  in  gelatin  mixture.  Chill  until  firm.  Yield:  one 
(9-inch)  pie.

3  egg  whites  6  Tbsp.  sugar 

1/4  tsp.  cream  of  tartar  1/2  tsp.  vanilla 

Mix  together  sugar,  cocoa,  salt  and  cornstarch.  Mix  in  egg 
yolks  and  milk.  Cook  until  mixture  thickens.  Add  margarine  and 
vanilla.  Pour  into  baked  pie  shells.  Top  with  meringue  and  bake  in 
325°  oven  until  lightly  browned. 

Meringue:  Have  egg  whites  at  room  temperature.  Add  cream  of 
tartar.  Beat  at  high  speed  until  egg  whites  are  foamy.  Slowly  add 
sugar  and  beat  until  whites  hold  a  stiff  peak.  Beat  in  vanilla. 
Spread  over  pie,  sealing  meringue  to  pie  shell.     Makes  2. 

Sarah  Lee 
Stella  Almond 

FUDGE  PECAN  PIE 

1/2  c.  butter  or  margarine  1  tsp.  vanilla 

3  Tbsp.  cocoa  1  small  can  evaporated  milk 
3/4  c.  hot  water  1  c.  pecan  halves 

2  c.  sugar  1  deep  dish  pie  crust 

1/2  c.  flour  1  c.  whipped  topping 

1/8  tsp.  salt 

Preheat  oven  and  cookie  sheet  to  350°.  In  medium  saucepan,  melt 
butter.  Add  cocoa  and  stir  until  dissolved.  Add  hot  water.  With  wire 
whip  blend  in  sugar  and  flour  mixture,  salt,  vanilla  and  evaporated 
milk.  Stir  until  batter  is  smooth.  Mix  in  pecans  and  pour  into  pie 
shell.  Bake  on  preheated  cookie  sheet  for  50  minutes  or  until  a  knife 
inserted  1-inch  from  the  edge  comes  out  clean.  Cool.  Serve  with 
whipped  cream  (optional). 

Jean  Riggins 

NUDGE'S  "OH  SO  GOOD  PIES"

1  stick  butter  1  c.  coconut 

1  Tbsp.  vinegar  2  (9-inch)  unbaked  pie  shells 

Cream  butter  and  sugar,  add  eggs  and  beat.  Mix  other  ingredi- 
ents and  pour  into  pie  shells.  Bake  at  350°  35  to  40  minutes  or  until 
done.    This  pie  freezes  well.

BROWN  SUGAR  PIE

PIE  CRUST 

2  1/2  c.  sifted  all-purpose  1  egg,  slightly  beaten 
flour  1/4  c.  cold  water 

1  tsp.  salt  1  Tbsp.  vinegar 

1  c.  shortening 

Mix  flour  and  salt;  cut  in  shortening  with  pastry  blender  until' 
mixture  looks  like  coarse  meal.  Add  egg,  water  and  vinegar  all  at  one 
time  and  mix  until  flour  is  moistened.  Form  into  a  ball,  divide  intol 
fourths  and  roll  out.      Dough     will     keep     in     refrigerator     for  several! 

weeks.    Makes  two  double  crust  pies.    Freezes  good.

HURRY-UP  BUTTERHORN  ROLLS 

1  pkg.  active  dry  yeast  2  1/2  c.  Bisquick 
3/4  c.  warm  water 

Dissolve  yeast  in  warm  water.  Stir  in  Bisquick.  Beat  vigorous- 
ly. Turn  onto  surface  dusted  with  Bisquick.  Knead  until  smooth, 
approximately  30  strokes.  Cover;  let  rest  10  minutes.  Roll  to  a 
12-inch  circle.  Cut  in  16  wedges.  Beginning  at  end,  roll  each  wedge 
toward  point.  Place  on  greased  baking  sheet,  point  side  down.  Cover 
with  damp  cloth,  let  rise  1  hour  until  doubled.  Bake  at  400"  10  to  15 
minutes.     Brush  with  butter  or  margarine  while  warm. 

Pat  Reid 

REFRIGERATOR  ROLLS 

2  pkg.  yeast  1/2  c.  sugar 
2  1/2  c.  warm  water                                    2  eggs 

3/4  c.  oil  7  to  7  1/2  c.  flour 

2  1/2tsp.  salt 

Add  yeast  to  warm  water  in  large  bowl.  Add  oil,  sugar,  eggs, 
salt  and  4  cups  flour.  Beat  until  smooth.  Stir  in  remaining  flour. 
Add  more  flour  if  needed.  Put  on  floured  surface.  Knead  until  smooth. 
Put  in  well  oiled  bowl.  Cover  and  refrigerate.  Next  day,  take  dough 
out,  punch  down  to  get  out  air  bubbles.  Pinch  off  what  you  need,  make 
into  rolls.     Dough  will  keep  in  refrigerator  for  3  days. 

Ella  H.  Maner 

QUICK  CHEESE  BREAD 

2  eggs  1  tsp.  dry  mustard 

3/4  c.  water  1  1/2  c.  grated  sharp  Cheddar 

2  (5  1/2  oz.)  pkg.  Martha  cheese 

White  Bix-Mix  2  Tbsp.  butter 

Preheat  oven  to  350°.  Grease  8  1/2x4  1/2-inch  loaf  pan.  Beat 
eggs  in  large  bowl,  stir  in  water  and  Bix-Mix  and  beat.  Add  mustard 
and  1  cup  of  the  cheese.  Mix  thoroughly.  Pour  batter  in  pan,  sprinkle 
with  remaining  cheese,  dot  with  butter.  Bake  for  45  minutes.  Let  cool 
before  slicing. 

Donna  Maner  Hargett

ONION  BREAD

1/2  c.  milk 


1  1/2  c.  Bisquick 

1  c.  sharp  Cheddar  cheese 

2  Tbsp.  melted  butter

milk  together.     Blend  in     Bisquick.    Add    onion    and     half    of    cheese.

cheese.     Sprinkle  with  butter.     Bake  for  20  to  25  minutes.

SALMON  SOUTHERN  CORNBREAD 


1  (7  3/4  oz.)  can  salmon 

1  c.  sifted  flour 

1  c.  corn  meal 

4  tsp.  baking  powder 

1/4  c.  sugar 


1/2  tsp.  salt 

1  egg,  beaten 

1  c.  salmon  liquid  and  milk 

1/4  c.  butter,  melted 


Drain  salmon,  reserving  liquid.  Flake  salmon.  Sift  together 
flour,  corn  meal,  baking  powder,  sugar  and  salt.  Combine  egg,  salmon 
liquid  and  butter.  Add  to  dry  ingredients  and  mix  just  enough  to 
moisten.  Stir  in  salmon.  Place  in  well-greased  baking  dish,  8  x  8  x 
2-inches.     Bake  in  hot  425°  oven  for  25  to  30  minutes. 

Sarah  C.  Skidmore

BANANA  SPICE  LOAF 


1  pkg.  spice  cake  mix 

1  pkg.  instant  vanilla  pudding 

4  eggs 

1  c.  water 

Topping: 

3/4  c.  brown  sugar 
1/2  c.  margarine 


1/3  c.  oil 

2  large  bananas 

1  c.  nut  meats 


1/2  c.  nut  meats 


Mix  eggs,  water,  oil,  bananas  and  nuts  in  blender.  Pour  over 
cake  mix  and  instant  pudding.  Stir  well.  Makes  2  loaves.  Line  pans 
with  foil.  Bake  at  350°  for  45  minutes.  Melt  topping  on  range.  Pour 
over  loaves  before  cool.

COFFEE  CAN  SALLY  LUNN 


4  c.  all-purpose  flour 
1  pkg.  yeast 
1/2  c.  milk 
1/2  c.  water 


1/2  c.  corn  oil 
1/4  c.  sugar 
11/2  tsp.  salt 
2  eggs,  beaten 


Preheat  oven  to  375°.  Grease  well  2  (1  pound)  coffee  cans  with 
lids. 

Combine  1/2  of  flour  and  yeast  in  large  mixing  bowl.  Heat  milk, 
water,  oil,  sugar  and  salt  until  warm.  Stir  well  to  dissolve.  Add  to 
flour  and  yeast  and  mix  well.  Beat  in  eggs.  Gradually  beat  in  rest  of 
flour     until     smooth     and  elastic,  about  5  minutes. 

Divide  into  coffee  cans.  Put  on  lids.  Let  rise  in  warm  place 
until  about  1-inch  from  top  of  can,  about  1  hour.  Take  off  lids  and 
bake  in  preheated  375°  oven  about  30  minutes  until  bread  is  puffed  and 
brown.    Let    cool  15  minutes  and  remove  from  cans.    Cover  top  with  foil

if  browning  too  quickly.     Serve  warm  with  butter  or  toast  it.     Good  for 

breakfast.
