Candy  Testing 


Thermometer  Test: 


Check  candy  thermometer  in  boiling  water.  If  it  doesn't  register 
212  degrees,  add  or  subtract  the  same  number  of  degrees  in 
recipe.  Always  make  sure  candy  thermometer  is  covered  with 
liquid,  not  just  foam.  Clip  it  to  the  side  of  the  pan  after  syrup 
boils. 


Cold-Water  Test:  Remove  candy  from  fire.  Drop  a  little  syrup  into  small  bowl  of 
very  cold,  but  not  ice  cold,  water.  Use  a  fresh  cupful  of  cold 
water  for  each  test.   Form  into  ball  with  fingers,  if  possible. 


CANDY 


DEGREES 


STAGE 


COLD  WATER  TEST 


230-234  degrees        Thread 


Fudge,  Fondant  234-240  degrees         Soft  Ball 


Syrup  spins  2-inch  thread 
when  dropped  from  spoon 

Candy  will  roll  into  soft 
ball  but  quickly  flattens 
when  removed  from  water 


Divinity,  Caramels        244-248  degrees         Firm  ball 


Candy  will  roll  into  a  firm 
ball  but  not  hard  ball 
which  will  not  lose  its 
shape  upon  removal  from 
water. 


Taffy 


Butterscotch 


250-266  degrees         Hard  ball 


270-290  degrees         Light  Crack 


Syrup  forms  hard  ball, 
although  it  is  pliable 

Candy  will  form  threads 
in  water  which  will  soften 
when  removed  from  water 


Peanut  Brittle  300-310  degrees         Hard  Crack 


Candy  will  form  hard, 
brittle  threads  in  water 
which  will  not  soften 
when  removed  from  water 


Caramelized  Sugar       310-321  degrees         Caramelized 


Sugar  first  melts,  then 
becomes  a  golden  brown 
and  will  form  a  hard, 
brittle  ball  in  cold  water

RED  VELVET  POUND  CAKE 

2  sticks  margarine  2  oz.  red  food  coloring 
1/2  c.  Crisco  3  c.  flour 

3  c.  sugar  1/2  tsp.  baking  powder 
5  eggs,  slightly  beaten  1  c.  milk 

1  tsp.  vanilla 

Cream  together  shortening  and  sugar.  Add  eggs,  vanilla  and  food 
coloring.  Mix  well.  Mix  alternately  with  this  mixture  the  flour  and 
milk;  ending  with  flour. 

Bake  in  tube  pan  for  1  hour  and  15  minutes.  Start  in  cold  oven. 
Bake  at  325°.    Ice  with  cream  cheese  icing. 

Ruth  Clayton 

FIVE  FLAVOR  POUND  CAKE 

3  c.  sugar  1  tsp.  butternut  flavoring 

2  sticks  margarine  1  tsp.  coconut  flavoring 

1/2  c.  Crisco  1  tsp.  rum  or  almond  flavoring 

5  eggs,  slightly  beaten  3  c.  unsifted  flour 

1  tsp.  lemon  flavoring  1  c.  milk 
1  tsp.  vanilla  flavoring 

Mix  sugar  and  shortenings.  Add  eggs  and  flavorings.  Mix  well. 
Alternately  add  flour  and  milk;  ending  with  flour.  Bake  in  tube  pan 
for  75  to  90  minutes.  Don't  open  oven  for  1  hour.  Start  with  a  cold 
oven.     Bake  at  325°. 

Ruth  Clayton

tube  pan.    Bake  at  325°  for  1  hour  and  20  minutes.

CARAMEL  NUT  POUND  CAKE

MRS.  BARRINGER'S  POUND  CAKE 

1  c.  butter,  packed  solid  1/2  tsp.  mace 

1  2/3  c.  granulated  sugar  2  c.  flour,  sifted 

5  unbeaten  eggs 

Have  a  round  pan  greased  and  floured.  Have  oven  heated  to  325 
Have  ingredients  measured  as  mixing  must  all  be  done  by  hand  or  at  very 
low  speed  on  mixer.  Cream  the  butter.  Add  sugar  and  work  until  ver 
light.  Add  spice  or  vanilla  and  1  egg  at  a  time  and  stir  until  th 
yolk  cannot  be  seen.  Then  add  another  egg  in  same  manner  until  all  are 
added.  Add  flour  mix  and  turn  at  once  into  pan.  Bake  slowly  about  a 
hour.

CREAM  CHEESE  POUND  CAKE 

1  c.  margarine,  softened  6  large  eggs

1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese,  2  tsp.  vanilla 

softened  3  c.  cake  flour 
3  c.  sugar 

Combine  margarine,  butter,  sugar  and  cream  cheese.  Beat  well. 
Add  salt  and  eggs,  one  at  a  time.  Beat  well  after  each  addition.  Add 
flour  and  vanilla.  Mix  well.  Pour  into  greased  and  floured  10-inch 
tube  pan.  Place  in  cold  oven.  Set  oven  at  275°.  Bake  1  1/2  hours  or 
until  tested  done.     Cool  in  pan.

BUNDT  POUND  CAKE 

2  sticks  butter  1/2  tsp.  baking  powder 
2  c.  sugar  (optional) 

2  c.  all-purpose  flour  1  tsp.  or  more  vanilla  or  any 
5  large  eggs  preferred  flavoring 

Have  all  ingredients  at  room  temperature  for  at  least  two  hours. 
Preheat  oven  to  350°.  Grease  and  flour  lightly  a  large  heavy  Bundt 
cake  pan.  Put  all  ingredients  into  large  bowl  of  mixer  at  one  time, 
(except  add  flavoring  after  mixing).  Beat  on  medium  speed  of  mixer  10 
minutes,  stopping  about  three  times  to  scrape  sides  of  bowl  and  beat- 
ers. Pour  into  pan.  Bake  at  350°  about  1  hour  or  until  tests  done. 
Cool  in  pan  on  rack  30  minutes  to  1  hour,  no  longer.  Turn  onto  rack  to 
cool. 

Jo  Avett 

ORANGE  CRUSH  POUND  CAKE

1/2  stick  butter  1  c.  Orange  Crush 

2  3/4  c.  sugar  1  tsp.  orange  flavoring 
5  eggs  1  tsp.  vanilla 

Cream     shortening,     butter    and  sugar.     Add  eggs,  one  at  a  time, 

mixing   well.      Add   Crush   alternately   with   sifted   flour.      Add  flavorings. 

Pour  into  greased  and  floured  9-inch  tube  pan.    Bake  at  325°  for  1  hour 
and  10  minutes. 

Frosting: 

1/2  stick  butter  1  tsp.  orange  flavoring 

1  (3  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese,  1  c.  powdered  sugar 
softened  1/2  tsp.  vanilla 

Cream  together  butter  and  cream  cheese.  Add  powdered  sugar  and 
flavorings.  Spread  over  warm  cake.  Sundrop  can  be  substituted  for 
Crush;  use  lemon  flavoring  instead  of  orange.

CARAMEL  NUT  CAKE 

6  eggs,  separated  1  1/2  c.  sugar 

1  tsp.  baking  powder  1  tsp.  vanilla 

2  c.  graham  cracker  crumbs  1  c.  chopped  walnuts 
1  Tbsp.  flour  1/4  c.  orange  juice 

1  c.  brown  sugar  1/4  c.  butter 

1  pt  whipping  cream  1/2  tsp.  vanilla 

2  eggs,  beaten 

Beat  yolks  well.  Combine  sugar  and  baking  powder  and  add  to 
yolks.  Add  1  teaspoon  vanilla.  Beat  whites  until  stiff  but  not  dry. 
Fold  into  yolk  mixture.  Fold  in  crumbs  and  nuts.  Pour  into  two 
(9-inch)  cake  pans,  greased  and  lined  with  waxed  paper.  Bake  at  325° 
for  30  to  35  minutes.  Cool.  Remove  from  pans.  Spread  layers  with 
whipped  cream.  Meanwhile,  combine  brown  sugar  and  flour  in  saucepan. 
Add  orange  juice,  butter  and  2  eggs.  Cook  over  low  heat  until  thick- 
ened. Stir  in  vanilla.  Cool.  Pour  over  cake,  letting  it  dribble  down 
sides.     Refrigerate  for  several  hours  before  serving. 

Katherine  Collins

CAKES,  COOKIES,  FROSTINGS  &  CONFECTIONS 


1/3  pkg.  dry  yeast  in  2  1/4  1/2  c.  cocoa 

Tbsp.  warm  water  1  small  can  evaporated  milk 

1/2  c.  soft  shortening  3/4  tsp.  baking  soda  in  2  1/2 
1  1/2  c.  sugar  Tbsp.  warm  water 

Sift  flour  before  measuring  and  add  salt.  Let  stand.  Soften 
yeast  in  2  1/2  tablespoons  warm  water.  Let  stand.  Put  shortening  in 
bowl.  Gradually  add  sugar,  mixing  until  light  and  fluffy.  Add  eggs 
and  vanilla.  Sift  cocoa  and  add  to  batter.  Add  flour  mixture  alter- 
nately with  milk,  beginning  and  ending  with  flour.  Beat  until  smooth 
after  each  addition.  Mix  in  softened  yeast.  Cover  and  refrigerate 
overnight. 

Next  morning,  preheat  oven  to  350°.  Grease  2  deep  8-inch  cake 
pans.  Dissolve  soda  in  2  1/2  tablespoons  warm  water.  Stir  into  cake 
mixture.  Pour  into  prepared  cake  pans.  Bake  30  minutes  or  until  cake 
shrinks  from  sides  of  pans.  Let  stand  5  minutes  before  turning  out. 
Frost  with  favorite  frosting. 

Laura  Frances  Young 

COCONUT  CAKE 

1  box  white  pudding  recipe  1  (7  oz.)  pkg.  Dover  Farms 

cake  mix  frozen  coconut 

1  c.  sugar  1  carton  Cool  Whip 
1  c.  milk 

Make  cake  according  to  package  directions.  Bake  in  rectangular 
pan.  Mix  milk  and  sugar  until  sugar  is  dissolved,  then  pour  over 
slightly  cooled  cake.  Sprinkle  with  coconut,  reserving  a  little  for 
the  top.  Then  spread  with  Cool  Whip  and  sprinkle  with  remaining 
coconut.     Keep  refrigerated. 

Mary  Ella  Vick

PINEAPPLE  CHIFFON  CAKE 

2  1/4  c.  all-purpose  flour  1  (8  1/4  oz.)  can  crushed 
1  1/2  c.  sugar,  divided  sweetened  pineapple 

1  Tbsp.  baking  powder  1  tsp.  lemon  peel 

1  tsp.  salt  1  Tbsp.  fresh  lemon  juice 

7  eggs,  separated  2  tsp.  vanilla  extract 

1/2  c.  vegetable  oil  1/2  tsp.  cream  of  tartar 

Combine  flour,  1  cup  sugar,  baking  powder  and  salt  in  mixing 
bowl.  Add  egg  yolks,  vegetable  oil,  undrained  pineapple,  grated  lemon 
peel,  lemon  juice  and  vanilla.  Beat  egg  whites  with  cream  of  tartar  to 
soft  peaks.  Slowly  beat  in  remaining  1/2  cup  sugar  until  stiff  peaks 
form.  Pour  pineapple  mixture  over  beaten  egg  whites;  fold  in  until 
completely  blended.  Pour  into  ungreased  10-inch  tube  pan.  Bake  on 
lowest  rack  in  325°  oven  65  to  70  minutes  until  cake  tests  done. 
Invert  pan  until  cake  has  completely  cooled. 

Gay  Hanback 

COLD  LEMON  CAKE 

1  box  lemon  cake  mix  with  1  small  can  frozen  lemonade 

pudding  1  (8  oz.)  container  Cool  Whip 

1  can  sweetened  condensed  milk 

Bake  cake  according  to  directions  making  3  layers.  Mix  remain- 
ing ingredients  for  filling.  When  cake  is  completely  cool,  stack  with 
filling  and  ice  with  same.  Refrigerate.  Best  when  made  a  couple  of 
days  before  using. 

Shirley  Cagle 

LEMON  PINEAPPLE  CHEESE  CAKE 

1  c.  sugar  1  box  lemon  jello 

1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese  1  c.  hot  water 


-78- 


CAKES,  COOKIES,  FROSTINGS  &  CONFECTIONS 


1  c.  crushed  pineapple, 

drained 
1  carton  whipped  topping 


32  graham  crackers 
1/4  c.  melted  butter 


Allow  cheese  to  soften  at  room  temperature,  then  add  sugar.  Mix 
jello  with  1  cup  hot  water,  let  cool.  Crush  graham  crackers,  add 
melted  butter  and  press  into  a  9  x  13-inch  dish.  Chill.  Mix  jello, 
pineapple,  cheese  mixture  and  whipped  topping.  Add  to  crumb  crust. 
Chill  well.     May  be  made  day  before. 

Ella  H.  Maner 


COFFEE  CAKE 


2  c.  sugar 

2  sticks  margarine 

2  eggs 

1  c.  sour  cream 

1  tsp.  vanilla 

Topping: 

4  Tbsp.  brown  sugar 
1  Tbsp.  cinnamon 


2  c.  flour 

1  tsp.  baking  soda 
1  tsp.  baking  powder 
1  tsp.  salt 


1  c.  chopped  pecans 
powdered  sugar 


Blend  sugar,  margarine  and  eggs  together.  Mix  well.  Slowly  and 
carefully  fold  in  sour  cream  and  vanilla.  Add  all  dry  ingredients. 
Spoon  1/2  of  batter  in  a  greased  and  floured  Bundt  pan  and  sprinkle 
with  1/2  of  the  topping.  Then  spoon  remainder  of  batter  and  topping. 
Bake  at  350°  for  50  to  60  minutes.  Let  cool  in  pan.  Turn  upside  down 
and  dust  with  powdered  sugar. 

Cindy  Beane 

SOUR  CREAM  COFFEE  CAKE 


1  c.  butter  (no  margarine) 

2  c.  sugar 
2  eggs 

1  c.  dairy  sour  cream 

Mix  Together: 

1  c.  chopped  pecans 
1  Tbsp.  plus  1  tsp.  sugar 


1/2  tsp.  vaniiia 

2  c.  all-purpose  flour 

1  tsp.  baking  powder 


1  tsp.  cinnamon 


Cream  butter  and  2  cups  sugar  until  light  and  fluffy.  Beat  in 
eggs,  one  at  a  time.  Fold  in  sour  cream.  Add  vanilla.  Mix  flour, 
baking  powder  and  salt.  Fold  into  batter.  Spread  1/3  batter  into 
greased  and  floured  8-inch  spring-form  pan.  Sprinkle  3/4  of  pecans, 
sugar  and    cinnamon    mixture    over    batter.    Add  remaining  batter.    Top 


63786 


-79- 


CAKES,  COOKIES,  FROSTINGS  &  CONFECTIONS 


with  remaining  nut  mixture.    Bake    at  325°  for  1  hour  and  20  minutes  or 
until  wooden  pick  comes  out  clean.    Cool  completely  on  wire  rack. 

Jean  Riggins 

BANANA  SPOT  CAKE 

1  c.  margarine  2  c.  graham  cracker  crumbs 

2  eggs  with  margarine 
1  box  powdered  sugar 

Mix  together  1  cup  margarine,  eggs  and  sugar  for  15  minutes. 
Mix  graham  cracker  cumbs  with  margarine.  Press  into  a  9  x  13-inch  pan. 
Spread  filling  on  crumbs.     Slice  three  bananas  on  top  of  filling. 

Drain  well  1  large  can  pineapple  and  spread  on  bananas. 

Prepare  2  packages  of  whipped  topping  and  spread  over  mixture. 
Sprinkle  with  chopped  nuts  and  place  in  refrigerator  for  three  hours 
before  serving.     Top  each  slice  with  cherries. 

Rachel  S.  Lowder 

EASY  PEANUT  BUTTER  COOKIES 

1  (14  oz.)  can  Eagle  Brand  2  c.  biscuit  mix 
milk  1  tsp.  vanilla 

3/4  c.  peanut  butter  sugar 

Beat  milk  and  peanut  butter  together  until  smooth.  Add  biscuit 
mix  and  vanilla  and  mix  well.  Shape  into  1-inch  balls,  roll  in  sugar 
and  place  2-inches  apart  on  ungreased  baking  sheet.  Flatten  with  fork. 
Bake  at  375°  for  6  to  8  minutes.    Makes  about  5  dozen. 

Ella  H.  Maner 

Brian  Bowers 

SWEDISH  BUTTERNUT  COOKIES 

2  c.  butter  or  margarine  4  1/2  c.  flour 

1  1/2  c.  sugar  1  egg  white,  slightly  beaten 

6  egg  yolks  1  c.  ground  walnuts 

1  tsp.  almond  extract 

Cream  together  butter  and  sugar  until  light  and  fluffy.  Blend 
in  egg  yolks  and  almond  extract.  Gradually  add  flour  to  creamed  i 
mixture;  mix  well.  Shape  dough  in  2-inch  strips  about  1/2-inch  thick. 
Dip  in  egg  white,  then  in  walnuts.  Place  2-inches  apart  on  ungreased 
baking  sheets.  Bake  in  425°  oven  about  8  minutes  or  until  golden 
brown.  Remove  from  baking  sheets.  Cool  on  racks.  Makes  12  dozen. 
Good  for  bridal  showers. 

Nell  Colson

PUMPKIN  COOKIES 


1/3  c.  shortening 
1  c.  sugar 

1  c.  pumpkin 

2  1/4  c.  flour 

4  tsp.  baking  powder 
1  tsp.  cinnamon 


1/4  tsp.  ginger 

1/4  tsp.  nutmeg 

1/4  tsp.  salt 

1/4  tsp.  vanilla 

1/2  tsp.  lemon  extract 

1/2  c.  black  walnuts 


Cream  shortening  and  sugar.  Add  pumpkin.  Mix  well.  Add  sifted 
dry  ingredients,  vanilla  and  lemon  extract.  Drop  onto  an  ungreased 
cookie  sheet.     Bake  in  375°  oven. 

Stella  Almond 


1-2-3-4  COOKIES 


1  c.  butter 

2  c.  sugar 

3  c.  flour 


4  eggs 

1  1/2  tsp.  baking  powder 

2  Tbsp.  warm  water 


Cream  butter  and  sugar  and  add  eggs  not  separated.  Sift  flour 
and  baking  powder  together.  Add  to  mixture  alternately  with  water. 
Add  flour  in  rolling  to  make  right  consistency.  Cut  with  biscuit 
cutter,  1/4-inch  thick  and  sprinkle  sugar  on  top.  Bake  in  moderate 
oven.     Do  not  pile  together  until  cold. 

Beth  Bowers 

THOMAS  JEFFERSON'S  BACHELOR  BUTTONS 


3/4  c.  butter,  softened 

1  3/4  c.  sugar 

2  eggs,  beaten 
1  tsp.  vanilla 

3  c.  plain  flour 


2  tsp.  baking  powder 
1/2  tsp.  salt 

maraschino  cherry  halves,  well 
drained 


Cream  butter  and  sugar;  add  eggs  and  vanilla,  beating  well. 
Sift  together  flour,  baking  powder  and  salt.  Add  to  creamed  mixture, 
mixing  well.  Drop  dough  by  teaspoonfuls  3-mches  apart  onto  greased 
cookie  sheets.  Press  a  cherry  half  in  center  of  each  cookie.  Bake  at 
375°  for  8  to  10  minutes.    Remove  from  cookie  sheets  and  cool. 

Ginger  Colson

CRISP  COCOA  COOKIES 

1  1/4  c.  plain  flour  1/2  c.  soft  butter  or 

1/2  tsp.  baking  soda  margarine 

1/4  tsp.  salt  1  egg 

1  c.  sugar  1  tsp.  vanilla 

1  c.  Cocoa  Krispies  cereal 

Preheat  oven  to  350°.  Lightly  grease  cookie  sheets.  Sift 
flour,  salt  and  soda  together;  set  aside.  In  large  bowl  cream  butter 
and  sugar  until  light  and  fluffy.  Add  egg;  mix  well.  Stir  in  flour 
mixture.  Drop  by  teaspoonfuls  2-inches  apart  on  cookie  sheets.  Bake 
12  minutes.  Remove  from  pan;  cool  on  wax  paper.  Store  in  airtight 
container.     Will  keep  a  long  time. 

Nell  Colson 

CAKE  MIX  COOKIES 

1  pkg.  cake  mix  (any  flavor)  1  egg 

2  Tbsp.  water 

Mix  with  a  fork  and  with  hands,  because  it's  a  very  stiff  dough. 
Place  small  balls  of  dough  on  an  ungreased  cookie  sheet  and  bake  for  8 
to  10  minutes  at  375°.     Yield:     4  dozen. 

Rolled  cookies  are  made  the  same  with  3  tablespoons  water 
instead  of  2. 

For  variation  add  any  of  the  following:  peanut  butter,  nuts, 
dates,  coconut  or  chocolate  chips. 

Mary  Louise  Colson 

KENTUCKY  COOKIES 

1  box  Keebler  graham  crackers  1  c.  chopped  almonds  or  pecans 

1  stick  butter  1/2  c.  white  sugar 

1  stick  margarine 

Butter  cookie  sheet  well.  Break  crackers  apart  and  line  on 
cookie  sheet  as  close  as  possible.  Melt  margarine  and  butter  slowly  in 
saucepan.  Turn  up  heat  and  bring  to  boil.  Add  sugar.  Boil  and  stir 
constantly  for  2  minutes.  Pour  over  crackers.  Sprinkle  nuts  over  all. 
Bake  in  325°  oven  for  11  or  12  minutes.  Remove  from  oven.  Place  on 
wax  paper  to  cool.    Separate  as  you  take  off  of  paper.    Makes  4  dozen. 

Margaret  Skidmore

CHOCOLATE  PECAN  COOKIES 

1  can  Eagle  Brand  sweetened  1  c.  all-purpose  flour 

milk  1  c.  chopped  nuts 

1  (12  oz.)  bag  chocolate  chips  1  tsp.  vanilla 

2  Tbsp.  butter 

Preheat  oven  to  350°.  Melt  milk,  chocolate  chips  and  butter  on 
low.  Add  and  mix  remaining  ingredients.  Drop  on  cookie  sheet.  Bake 
for  5  minutes. 

Robbie  Vaughn 

CHOCOLATE  CHIP  COOKIES 

2/3  c.  shortening  3  c.  plain  flour 

2/3  c.  butter  or  margarine,  1  tsp.  soda 

softened  1  tsp.  salt 

1  c.  granulated  sugar  1  c.  chopped  nuts 

1  c.  brown  sugar,  packed  2  (6  oz.)  pkg.  semi-sweet 

2  eggs  chocolate  pieces 
2  tsp.  vanilla 

Heat  oven  to  375°.  Mix  thoroughly  shortening,  butter,  sugars, 
eggs  and  vanilla.  Stir  in  remaining  ingredients.  (For  softer,  rounder 
cookies  add  1/2  cup  flour.) 

Drop  dough  by  rounded  teaspoonfuls  2-inches  apart  onto  ungreased 
baking  sheet.  Bake  8  to  10  minutes  or  until  light  brown.  Cook  slight- 
ly before  removing  from  baking  sheet.    Yields  about  7  dozen  cookies. 

Marianne  Bumgarner-Davis 
Ginger  Col  son 

ORANGE-OATMEAL  COOKIE  BARS 

1/2  c.  vegetable  shortening  grated  rind  of  one  orange 

1/4  c.  margarine  3/4  c.  chopped  pecans 

3/4  c.  firmly  packed  brown  3  c.  quick  cooking  oats, 

sugar  uncooked 

3/4  c.  granulated  sugar  1  c.  all-purpose  flour 

1  egg  1/2  tsp.  baking  soda 

1/4  c.  orange  juice  1/2  tsp.  salt 
1  tsp.  vanilla 

Preheat  oven  to  350°.  In  large  bowl,  cream  together  shortening 
and  margarine.  Beat  in  sugars,  egg,  orange  juice  and  vanilla  until 
smooth  and  well  beaten.  Mix  in  orange  rind  and  chopped  nuts.  Add 
remaining  ingredients  and  stir  until  thoroughly  mixed.  Smooth  into 
greased  13  x  9  x  2-inch  pan.  Bake  at  350°  for  30  minutes.  Remove  from 
oven  and  cut  into  squares  while  warm.  Allow  to  cool  and  remove  from 
pan.    Makes  approximately  35  (1   1/2-inch)  squares. 

For  drop    cookies,     drop     by    generous  teaspoonfuls  onto  greased

cookie  sheets.    Bake   about    14  minutes  at  350°.    Makes  approximately  4 
1/2  to  5  dozen. 

Elisabeth  Penry 

CREAM  CHEESE  COOKIE  BARS 

1  box  yellow  cake  mix  1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese 

1  stick  margarine,  melted  1  box  powdered  sugar 

3  eggs 

Blend  cake  mix,  margarine  and  1  egg  by  hand.  Mixture  will  be 
very  thick.  Spread  into  bottom  of  9  x  12-inch  pan.  Press  with  hands, 
if  necessary.  Blend  cream  cheese,  2  eggs  and  powdered  sugar  with 
mixer.  Pour  over  first  layer.  Bake  at  350°  for  45  minutes.  For 
variation,  try  other  cake  mix  flavors. 

Pam  Lisenby 

MERINGUE  COOKIES 

2  egg  whites  1  c.  nuts  or  chocolate  chips 
3/4  c.  sugar 

Preheat  oven  to  350°.  In  a  metal  bowl,  beat  egg  whites  until 
they  hold  a  peak.  Add  2  tablespoons  sugar  at  a  time  and  beat  until 
glossy  and  still  holds  a  peak.  Fold  in  one  cup  of  nuts  or  chocolate 
chips.  Spoon  onto  ungreased  cookie  sheet  1-inch  apart.  Place  in  oven 
and  turn  oven  off.  Leave  for  several  hours  or  overnight.  Keep  in  an 
airtight  container. 

Pam  Lisenby 

PECAN  COOKIE  SQUARES 

3/4  c.  brown  sugar  1  c.  flour 

1/2  c.  mayonnaise  1  tsp.  baking  powder 

1  tsp.  vanilla  3/4  c.  chopped  pecans 

Mix  sugar,  vanilla,  mayonnaise  and  vanilla  until  blended.  Stir 
in  flour,  baking  powder  and  1/2  cup  pecans.  Press  into  square  8-inch 
baking  pan.  Press  remaining  pecans  into  dough.  Bake  15  minutes  at 
350°.  Cool.  Cut  into  squares,  approximately  12  squares.  Recipe  can 
be  doubled. 

Betty  Walton 

CRISP  SUGAR  COOKIES 

2  c.  sugar  1  tsp.  salt 

1  c.  butter  or  margarine  1  tsp.  baking  soda 

4  eggs  2  Tbsp.  milk 

4  1/2  c.  sifted  flour  1  1/2  tsp.  vanilla,  coconut  or 

2  tsp.  baking  powder  lemon  flavoring 


-84- 


CAKES,  COOKIES,  FROSTINGS  &  CONFECTIONS 


Cream  together  sugar  and  shortening.  Add  eggs  one  at  a  time. 
Beat  well.  Sift  together  dry  ingredients.  Add  dry  ingredients  alter- 
nately with  milk  to  creamed  mixture.  Mix  well.  Chill  dough  in  refrig- 
erator 3  hours  or  overnight. 

Roll  dough  to  1/4-inch  thick  on  floured  surface.  Cut  with 
floured  cookie  cutter.  Place  2-inches  apart  on  greased  cookie  sheet. 
Bake  in  400°  oven  10  minutes  or  until  golden  brown.  Cool  about  a 
minute  before  removing  from  cookie  sheet.

OLD-FASHIONED  OATMEAL  COOKIES 

1  c.  raisins  1  tsp.  baking  soda 

1  c.  water  1  tsp.  salt 

3/4  c.  shortening  1  tsp.  cinnamon 

1  1/2  c.  sugar  1/2  tsp.  baking  powder 

2  eggs  1/2  tsp.  cloves 

1  tsp.  vanilla  2  c.  oats 

2  1/2  c.  flour  1/2  c.  chopped  walnuts 

Simmer  raisins  and  water  over  medium  heat  until  raisins  are 
plump,  about  15  minutes.  Drain  raisins,  reserving  the  liquid.  Add 
enough  water  to  reserved  liquid  to  measure  1/2  cup.  Cream  together 
thoroughly  shortening,  sugar,  eggs  and  vanilla.  Blend  in  raisin 
liquid.  Stir  in  remaining  ingredients.  Drop  dough  by  rounded  tea- 
spoonfuls  about  2-inches  apart  onto  ungreased  baking  sheet.  Bake  8  to 
10  minutes  in  400°  oven  or  until  light  brown.  Immediately  remove 
cookies  from  baking  sheet. 

Gay  Hanback 

OATMEAL  DATE  COOKIES 

1  c.  Crisco  shortening  1/2  tsp.  salt 

1  c.  brown  sugar  2  c.  quick-cooking  oats 

1  c.  white  sugar  1  c.  coconut 

3  eggs  1/2  c.  chopped  walnuts  or 

2  c.  flour,  sifted  pecans 

1  tsp.  baking  powder  1  c.  chopped  dates 

3/4  tsp.  baking  soda  1  tsp.  vanilla 

Cream  shortening  and  sugars  together  until  light  and  fluffy. 
Add  eggs.  Beat  well.  Blend  in  vanilla.  Sift  together  flour,  salt, 
baking  soda  and  baking  powder.  Add  gradually  to  creamed  mixture.  Mix 
well.  Stir  in  oats,  coconut,  nuts  and  dates.  Drop  by  teaspoonfuls 
about  2-inches  apart  on  greased  cookie  sheets.  Flatten  with  bottom  of 
glass  dipped  in  sugar.  Bake  in  375°  oven  8  minutes  or  until  lightly 
browned.     Makes  5  dozen. 

Nell  Colson

COOKIES  FOR  DIABETICS 

1  1/4  c.  water  1/3  c.  salad  oil  or  margarine 

2  c.  seedless  raisins  2  tsp.  cinnamon 
2  eggs,  beaten  1/2  tsp.  nutmeg 
2  tsp.  liquid  sweetener  2  Tbsp.  water 

1  tsp.  baking  powder  1  tsp.  soda 

1/2  tsp.  salt  2  c.  flour 

Combine  1  1/4  cup  water,  oil,  raisins,  cinnamon  and  nutmeg. 
Boil  together  for  3  minutes.  Cool.  Dissolve  salt,  soda  and  sweetener 
in  2  tablespoons  water  and  add  to  beaten  eggs.  Stir  into  the  cooled 
raisin  mixture.  Mix  well.  Add  nuts  and  drop  by  spoonfuls  onto  a 
greased  cookie  sheet.     Bake  at  350°  until  light  brown. 

Nell  Colson 

CREAM  CHEESE  ICING 

1  stick  margarine  1  box  powdered  sugar 

1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese  2  tsp.  vanilla 

Cream  margarine  and  cream  cheese.  Mix  in  sugar  and  vanilla; 
beat  well. 

Note:     Only  1/2  recipe  is  needed  for  tube  cake. 

Nancy  Vick  McSwain

PECAN  ROLLS

Creme 
1  box  powdered  sugar 
1  tsp.  vanilla  or  almond 

flavoring 


1/4  tsp.  butter  flavoring 

1  (14  oz.)  bag  caramels 

2  Tbsp.  canned  milk 
chopped  pecans 


Mix  Marshmallow  Creme,  powdered  sugar,  vaniila  or  almond  flavor- 
ing and  butter  flavoring  and  form  into  8  logs.  Wrap  in  plastic  wrap 
and  place  in  freezer.  In  double  boiler  melt  caramels  with  milk.  Roll 
logs  in  caramel  then  in  chopped  pecans. 

Margaret  Lisenby 

Nancy  Lisenby 


PEANUT  BRITTLE 


2  c.  sugar 

2  c.  raw  peanuts 

1  c.  Karo  syrup 


1/2  c.  water 

1  Tbsp.  baking  soda 


Using  candy  thermometer,  mix  and  cook  to  300°  all  ingredients 
except  soda.  At  300°  add  soda  and  stir  quickly.  Pour  onto  greased 
surface  and  stretch  and  break  into  pieces  as  it  cools. 

John  W.  Thompson 


CREAM  CHEESE  MINTS 


2  1/2  c.  powdered  sugar, 
sifted 


3  oz.  cream  cheese 

1/2  tsp.  peppermint  flavoring 


Mix  together  sugar,  cream  cheese  and  flavoring.  Mix  and  knead 
as  you  would  for  a  biscuit  dough.  Roll  dough  into  long  finger-size 
rolls  and  cut  into  1/2-inch  pieces.  Allow  mints  to  stand  uncovered  at 
room  temperature  overnight  or  until  they  dry  out  somewhat  and  crust 
forms  on  top.  Cover  in  a  tin  box  and  store  or  freeze.  (The  candy 
dough  may  also  be  rolled  out  like  a  pie  dough  and  cut  with  tiny  round 
cutters,  then  decorated  with  icing,  if  desired.) 

Pat  Reid 

HOLIDAY  FUDGE 

4  1/2  c.  sugar  1  (7  or  8  oz.)  jar  marshmallow 

pinch  of  salt  cream 

1/2  lb.  butter  2  c.  nuts 

1  large  can  evaporated  milk  1  tsp.  vanilla 

3  (6  oz.)  pkg.  semi-sweet  chocolate  chips 


63786 


■87- 


DESSERTS 

Mix  sugar,  salt,  butter  and  evaporated  milk.  Bring  to  boil, 
stirring  constantly.  Then  boil  8  1/2  minutes  without  stirring.  Remove 
from  heat.  Add  chocolate.  When  melted  add  marshmallow  cream,  nuts  and 
vanilla.  Mix  well.  Pour  in  large  Pyrex  dish.  Let  stand  several  hours 
to  set.    Makes  about  5  pounds. 

Margaret  Lisenby 

RUBY'S  PEANUT  BUTTER  FUDGE 

2/3  c.  milk  pinch  of  salt 

1  Tbsp.  vanilla  2  Tbsp.  butter 

2  c.  sugar  1/3  c.  peanut  butter 
1/4  c.  cocoa 

Mix  milk,  vanilla,  sugar,  salt  and  cocoa.  Bring  to  a  soft 
bubbly  boil.  Cook  until  it  bubbles  if  one  drop  is  dropped  in  cold

MILKY  WAY  ICE  CREAM 

8  Milky  Way  bars  1  1/2  c.  sugar 

2  c.  milk  2  tsp.  vanilla 

6  eggs  2  large  cans  evaporated  milk 

Melt  Milky  Ways  in  milk  in  double  boiler  or  over  very  low  heat 
in  heavy  saucepan.  Cool.  While  mixture  is  cooling,  beat  eggs  until 
softly  piled.  Add  sugar;  beat  well.  Add  vanilla  and  evaporated  milk. 
Fold  in  Milky  Way  mixture.  Mix  well.  Pour  into  1  gallon  ice  cream 
freezer.  Add  milk  to  fill  freezer.  Mix  well.  Freeze  according  to 
freezer  directions. 

Stella  Almond

GERMAN  CHOCOLATE  ICE  CREAM 

2  (13  oz.)  cans  evaporated  1  c.  sugar 

milk  1  c.  pecans,  toasted  and 

2  oz.  chocolate  chopped 

1  (12  oz.)  jar  caramel  topping  1/2  c.  coconut  (optional) 

1  egg 

Combine  1  can  milk  and  chocolate  in  small  saucepan.  Cook  over 
medium  heat,  stirring  until  chocolate  melts.  Add  caramel  and  cook 
until  melted.  Remove  from  heat.  Beat  eggs  and  sugar  in  large  mixing 
bowl.  Stir  in  chocolate  mixture.  (Add  coconut,  optional.)  Stir  in 
i  remaining  can  of  milk.  Refrigerate  until  well  chilled.  Freeze  in  ice 
cream  freezer.     Sprinkle  nuts  on  top  to  serve.

I  LEMON  CHEESECAKE  ICE  CREAM 

1  c.  cottage  cheese  1/2  tsp.  grated  lemon  peel 

1/3  c.  freshly  squeezed  lemon  1/2  tsp.  vanilla 

|       juice  2  c.  half  and  half 

3  egg  yolks  3  egg  whites 
'    3/4  c.  sugar 

In  a  blender,  puree  cottage  cheese  and  lemon  juice  until  smooth; 
set  aside.  In  a  medium  bowl,  beat  egg  yolks  and  sugar  until  smooth  and 
thick.  Stir  in  pureed  cottage  cheese  mixture,  lemon  peel,  vanilla  and 
half  and  half;  set  aside.  In  medium  bowl,  beat  egg  whites  until  stiff 
but  not  dry.  Fold  into  egg  yolk  mixture.  Pour  into  ice  cream  canis- 
ter.    Freeze.     Makes  2  quarts. 

Sarah  Lee

MR.  GARRETT'S  POPCORN  BALLS

1  c.  brown  sugar 

1/3  c.  dark  molasses  or  Karo 

syrup 
1/3  c.  water 


1  Tbsp.  vinegar 

2  Tbsp.  butter 
1/8  tsp.  soda 
1/2  tsp.  vanilla 
1  can  coconut 

1/2  box  Rice  Krispies 


Mix  sugar,  molasses,  water,  vinegar  and  butter.  Boil  gently 
without  stirring  until  hard  ball  is  formed  in  cold  water.  Add  soda  and

Krispies.     Form  into  balls  while  warm.     Yield:     8  large  popcorn  balls.

BUTTERNUT  BALLS

1/4  c.  sugar  powdered  sugar 

1/2  tsp.  salt 

Sift  flour,  sugar  and  salt.  Add  butter,  softened,  and  vanilla.

CONGO  SQUARES 

2/3  c.  margarine  1/4  tsp.  salt 

1  box  dark  brown  sugar  3  eggs 

2  3/4  c.  plain  flour  2/3  pkg.  chocolate  chips 
2  1/2  tsp.  baking  powder  1  c.  nuts 

Melt  2/3  cup  margarine.  Add  1  box  dark  brown  sugar.  Mix  well 
and  set  to  cool.  Sift  together  flour,  baking  powder  and  salt.  To 
margarine-sugar  mixture  add  3  eggs,  beating  after  each  one.  Add  dry 
ingredients.  Mix  well.  Add  2/3  package  chocolate  chips  and  1  cup 
nuts.  Toss  lightly.  Bake  25  minutes  at  350°  on  a  well-greased  cake 
pan  or  two  8  x  8-inch  pans. 

Sam  Ussery 

BUTTERSCOTCH  SQUARES 

1  stick  butter  1  tsp.  baking  powder 

1  egg  1/4  tsp.  salt 

1  c.  brown  sugar  1  tsp.  vanilla 

1  c.  flour  1  c.  nuts 

Melt  one  stick  of  butter  in  pan.  Beat  1  egg.  Add  1  cup  brown 
sugar  and  cream  together.  Pour  melted  butter  over  mixture.  Add  1  cup 
flour,  1  teaspoon  baking  powder,  1/4  teaspoon  salt,  1  teaspoon  vanilla 
and  1  cup  nuts.  Bake  in  pan  that  the  butter  was  melted  in  for  25  or  30 
minutes  in  300°  oven. 

Rachel  S.  Lowder

NILLA  FRUIT  ROLLS 


1  c.  margarine 

2  c.  flour 

1/2  c.  sour  cream 
1  egg,  separated 
30  Nilla  wafers,  crushed  (about  1  c.) 


1/2  c.  coconut 
1  (6  oz.)  pkg.  pecan  halves 
18  oz.  apricot  preserves 
confectioners  sugar  glaze 


In  medium  bowl  cut  margarine  into  flour  until  crumbly.  Combine 
sour  cream  and  egg  yolk;  blend  into  flour  mixture  to  form  a  soft  dough. 
Divide  dough  into  4  equal  parts;  wrap  separately  and  refrigerate 
several  hours  or  overnight. 

Set  aside  48  pecan  halves;  chop  remaining  nuts  and  combine  with 
Nilla  crumbs  and  coconut.  On  well-floured  pastry  cloth,  roll  one 
portion  of  chilled  dough  into  12-inch  square.  Spread  1/3  cup  of 
preserves;  sprinkle  with  1/4  crumb  mix.  Roll  like  jellyroll.  Place  on 
ungreased  baking  sheet.  Cut  3/4  of  way  through  at  1-inch  intervals 
making  12  sections.  Complete  other  3  rolls  the  same.  Brush  with 
beaten  egg  white.  Bake  at  350°  for  35  to  40  minutes.  Cool.  Top  with 
pecan  half  on  each  section  and  drizzle  with  confectioners  sugar  glaze. 

Julian  Trail,  Jr.

FROZEN  STRAWBERRY  DESSERT 


1  c.  flour 

1/4  c.  brown  sugar 

1/2  c.  walnuts  or  pecans, 

chopped 
1/2  c.  butter,  melted 

2  egg  whites,  beaten  stiff 
1  c.  granulated  sugar 


2  Tbsp.  lemon  juice 

1  c.  whipped  cream  or  Cool 
Whip 

2  c.  sliced  fresh  strawberries 
or  1  (10  oz.)  pkg.  frozen 
strawberries 

2/3  c.  sugar 


Mix  flour,  brown  sugar,  walnuts  or  pecans  and  butter  together. 
Spread  in  shallow  pan.  Bake  at  350°  for  20  minutes,  stirring  occasion- 
ally. Sprinkle  2/3  of  the  crumbs  in  13  x  9  x  2-inch  baking  pan. 
Combine  egg  whites  (beaten)  granulated  sugar,  berries  and  lemon  juice 
in  large  bowl  and  beat  at  high  speed  to  form  stiff  peaks  (10  minutes). 
Fold  in  whipped  cream,  spoon  over  crumbs,  top  with  remaining  crumbs. 
Freeze  overnight  or  6  hours.  Garnish  with  whole  berries  (optional). 
Serves  8. 

Mary  Jane  Komlos

Jell-O

pinch  of  salt

torn  in  pieces

in  Cool  Whip.  Cover  bottom  of  9  x  13-inch  pan  with  cake  pieces;  pour

to  set.     Yield:     10  to  15  servings.

1/2  tsp.  salt 


1/2  c.  nutmeats 
1  c.  hot  water 
1  tsp.  soda 
1  c.  brown  sugar 
1  c.  hot  water 
1  Tbsp.  oleo 


Cut  up  dates  and  soak  in  hot  water.  When  cool  add  soda. 
Prepare  9  x  13-inch  baking  pan  with  brown  sugar,  hot  water  and  oleo. 

Cream  sugar  and  shortening.  Add  egg  and  mix.  Add  dry  ingredi- 
ents alternately  with  date  mixture.  Stir  in  nuts.  Pour  into  pan.  DO 
NOT  stir  mixture  into  liquid.  As  it  bakes  it  forms  a  thick  sauce  on 
the  bottom  of  the  pudding.  Good  served  hot  or  cold  and  with  a  dollop 
of  whipped  topping.     Baking  time:    30  minutes  at  350°. 

Evelyn  Norwood 

CHOCOLATE  DESSERT 


1  c.  plain  flour 

1  stick  margarine 

1/2  c.  nuts 

1  c.  powdered  sugar 

1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese 


1  large  container  Cool  Whip 

2  small  pkg.  instant  chocolate 
pudding 

3  c.  cold  milk 


Let  margarine  soften  and  work  together  flour,  margarine  and 
nuts.  Press  into  square  or  round  pan  deeper  than  pie  pan.  Bake  20 
minutes    at    300°.    Allow    crust  to  cool. 

Mix  together  powdered  sugar,  cream  cheese  and  1/2  container  Cool 
Whip.  Spoon  into  pan  on  top  of  crust  and  level  with  spoon.  Then  mix 
the  2  packages  pudding  with  the  3  cups  milk  until  slightly  thickened. 
Add  as  next  layer.  Spread  remaining  Cool  Whip  on  top  and  sprinkle  with 
nuts,  if  desired. 

Note:  For  variation  use  instant  lemon  or  butterscotch  pudding. 
For  a  lighter  chocolate,  use  1  package  chocolate  and  1  package  vanilla 
pudding. 

Pam  Lisenby 


BUTTERSCOTCH  TORTE 


1  1/2  c.  plain  flour 
1  1/2  sticks  margarine 


1  small  (8  oz.)  Cool  Whip 

2  instant  butterscotch  pudding 


■96- 


DESSERTS 

1  c.  chopped  nuts  3  c.  milk 

1  1/4  c.  powdered  sugar  1  large  Cool  Whip 

8  oz.  cream  cheese  1/4  to  1/2  c.  chopped  nuts 

Mix  flour,  margarine  and  nuts.  Press  into  bottom  of  13  x  9-inch 
pan.    Bake    20    minutes    at  350°.    Cool. 

Cream  sugar  and  cream  cheese.  Fold  in  8  ounces  Cool  Whip  and 
spread  over  baked  crust.  Mix  pudding  and  milk.  Pour  over  cheese  layer 
and  chill  until  sets.  Spread  1  large  Cool  Whip  on  top.  Sprinkle  with 
1/4  to  1/2  cup  nuts. 

Carolyn  Trail 

CHIPS  'N  MAC  DELIGHT 

2  pkg.  Chips  'n  Mac  cookies  Cool  Whip  or  whipped  cream 
(Jacks)  milk 

Dip  cookies  lightly  in  milk  (one  at  a  time).  Line  bottom  of  a 
deep  serving  dish  with  cookies.  Cover  cookies  with  a  1-inch  layer  of 
cream  or  Cool  Whip.  Add  another  layer  of  cookies  and  cover  with 
another  layer  of  cream  until  dish  is  full.  Chill  in  refrigerator  24 
hours  or  in  freezer  2  hours.     May  be  cut  in  squares. 

Mary  Frances  Colson 

CHOCOLATE  ECLAIR  CAKE 

2  (3  3/4  oz.)  pkg.  French  1  (9  oz.)  container  whipped 
instant  vanilla  pudding  topping 

3  c.  milk  graham  crackers 

Chocolate  Topping: 

1/4  c.  milk  1/8  tsp.  salt 

1/3  c.  cocoa  1/4  stick  margarine 

1  c.  sugar  1  tsp.  vanilla 

Combine  pudding  mix  and  milk.  Mix  well.  Fold  in  thawed  whipped 
topping  and  beat  two  minutes  at  medium  speed.  Butter  a  9  x  13-inch 
dish.  Place  layer  of  whole  graham  crackers  in  dish.  Spread  one-half 
of  pudding  mixture  over  crackers.  Top  with  second  layer  of  graham 
crackers.  Spread  remaining  half  of  pudding  mixture  over  crackers.  Top 
with  third  layer  of  crackers.  Pour  cooled  chocolate  topping  over  cake. 
Refrigerate  until  ready  to  serve. 

Chocolate  Topping:  Combine  milk,  cocoa,  sugar  and  salt  in 
saucepan.  Boil  one  minute.  Remove  from  heat,  add  margarine  and 
vanilla.    Cool.    Top  cake. 

Pat  Reid

CHEW  BREAD 


1  stick  margarine 

1  box  light  brown  sugar 
3  eggs

1  tsp.  vanilla 

nuts,  coconut  and  chocolate 
chips 


Cream  sugar  and  margarine.  Add  eggs,  one  at  a  time,  beating 
well  after  each  one.  Add  flour  and  vanilla.  Fold  in  other  ingredi-

DELICIOUS  BROWNIES 

1  c.  butter  dash  of  salt 

2  c.  sugar  1  Tbsp.  vanilla 
4  eggs  nuts 

1/2  c.  cocoa  6  oz.  bag  marshmallows 

1  c.  plain  flour 

Topping: 

1  stick  margarine  1  tsp.  vanilla 

1  box  10x  powdered  sugar  1/3  c.  cream 

3  Tbsp.  cocoa  (heaping) 

Beat  butter  and  sugar  until  creamy.  Add  eggs,  one  at  a  time, 
beating  until  lemon  colored.  Add  cocoa,  flour,  salt  and  vanilla.  Beat 
until  smooth.  Pour  into  9  x  13-inch  or  larger  pan.  Sprinkle  nuts  over 
top.  Bake  at  325°  for  25  minutes.  Should  not  be  crusty,  should  remain 
moist,  but  toothpick  in  center  should  come  out  clean.  Pour  on  marsh- 
mallows  when  removed  from  oven.    Pour  on  topping  while  still  warm. 

Topping:  Put  all  in  small  mixer  bowl.  Beat  on  high  speed  until 
smooth.    Pour  over  brownies  while  they  are  warm.    Cool  and  slice. 

Claudette  Kayler

PETITE  CHERRY  CHEESECAKES 


24  vanilla  wafers 

2  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese, 

softened 
3/4  c.  sugar 
2  eggs 


1  Tbsp.  lemon  juice 
1  tsp.  vanilla 

1  (1  lb.  5  oz.)  can  cherry  pie 
filling 


Beat  together  cream  cheese,  softened,  sugar,  2  eggs,  lemon  juice 
and  vanilla  until  light  and  fluffy.  Line  small  muffin  pans  with  24 
paper  cups;  place  a  vanilla  wafer  in  the  bottom  of  each.  Fill  cups  2/3 
full  with  cheese  mixture.  Bake  at  375°  for  15  to  20  minutes  or  just 
until  set.  Top  with  1  tablespoon  cherry  pie  filling.  Chill.  Makes  2 
dozen  cakes. 

Sarah  Lee 


CHEESE  CAKE 


2  c.  graham  cracker  crumbs 

2  sticks  margarine 

2  Tbsp.  powdered  sugar 

2  pkg.  lemon  jello 

10  oz.  boiling  water 

10  oz.  cold  water 


2  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese 

(room  temperature) 
2  c.  sugar 

1  Tbsp.  plus  1  tsp.  vanilla 

2  large  cans  Pet  milk 


Place  milk  in  refrigerator  for  24  hours  before  using.  Dissolve 
jello  in  10  ounces  of  boiling  water;  add  cold  water  and  place  in 
refrigerator  until  cool.  DO  NOT  LET  CONGEAL.  Whip  milk  by  hand  until 
it  gets  thick  and  foamy;  do  not  whip  too  long.  Mix  cream  cheese  well. 
Add    sugar    and    vanilla    and    blend. 

Melt  margarine;  add  crumbs  and  powdered  sugar  to  make  crust. 
Mix  chilled  jello  mixture  with  cheese  mixture.  Blend  well.  Put  crust 
in  bottom  of  dish  and  pour  other  mixture  on  top.     Chill. 

Richard  Lisenby

DESSERTS 


PETRA'S  DELICIOUS  CHEESECAKE 


1  small  pkg.  lemon  jello 

1  c.  boiling  water 

3  Tbsp.  lemon  juice 

1  (8  oz.)  pkg.  cream  cheese 

3/4  c.  sugar 

1/2  tsp.  vanilla 


1  tall  can  evaporated  milk, 

chilled 
1  lb.  pkg.  graham  cracker 

crumbs 
1/2  c.  butter 


Dissolve  jello  in  boiling  water.  Add  lemon  juice  and  cool. 
Cream  together  cream  cheese,  sugar  and  vanilla.  Add  jello  and  mix 
well.     Whip  evaporated  milk  and  fold  into  jello  mixture. 

Add  butter  to  graham  cracker  crumbs.  Mix  well.  Line  pan  with 
graham  cracker  crust.  Add  filling.  Sprinkle  remaining  crumbs  on  top 
for  garnish.     Chill  until  firm.     Makes  2  (8  or  9-inch)  pie  plates. 

Mildred  Norwood

Helpful  Cooking  Hints 


Frozen  gravies  or  sauces  may  be  a  little 
thicker  after  thawing  than  when  they 
were  freshly  made.  Adding  a  little 
appropriate  liquid  -  milk,  broth,  bouillon 
or  wine  -  will  thin  them  to  the  desired 
consistency. 

For  extra  juicy,  extra  nutritious  hambur- 
gers, add  Va  cup  evaporated  milk  per 
pound  of  meat  before  shaping. 

To  ripen  green  pears,  just  place  2  or  3  in  a 
brown  bag,  loosely  closed,  and  store  at 
room  temperature  out  of  direct  sunlight. 

In  making  pickles,  use  white  vinegar  to 
make  clear  pickles  and  coarse  salt  that 
which  comes  in  5  pound  bags.  This  is  not 
rock  salt.  Avoid  using  iodized  salt  for 
pickle  making.  Most  pickles  are  better  if 
allowed  to  stand  six  weeks  before  using. 

Lemon  jello  dissolved  in  2  cups  of  hot 
apricot  nectar  with  1  teaspoon  of  grated 
lemon  added  for  zip  makes  a  perfect  base 
for  jelled  fruit  salad. 

Put  a  tablespoon  of  butter  in  the  water 
when  cooking  rice,  dried  beans,  maca- 
roni, to  keep  it  from  boiling  over.  Always 
run  cold  water  over  it  when  done  to  get 
the  starch  out.  Reheat  over  hot  water,  if 
necessary. 

A  pair  of  scissors  (not  the  fowl  kind  -  they 
are  heavy  and  awkward  to  handle)  fine  for 
slivering  celery,  onion,  meats,  and 
cheese. 

Never  put  a  cover  on  anything  that  is 
cooked  in  milk  unless  you  want  to  spend 
hours  cleaning  up  the  stove  when  it  boils 
over. 

Anything  that  grows  under  the  ground 
start  off  in  cold  water  -  potatoes  -  beets  - 
carrots  -  etc.  Anything  that  grows  above 
ground,  start  off  in  boiling  water  - 
English  peas  -  greens  -  beans,  etc. 

To  clean  aluminum  pots  when  they  are 
stained  dark,  merely  boil  with  a  little 
cream  of  tarter,  vinegar  or  acid  foods. 

Baking  powder  will  remove  tea  or  coffee 
stains  from  china  pots  or  cups. 


Learn  where  your  fuse  box  and  master 
cut-off  switch  is.  If  you  know  where  the 
lever  is  to  pull  you  can  always  cut  the 
current  off  until  a  service  man  can  come. 

Canned  cream  soups  make  excellent 
sauces  for  vegetables,  fish,  etc.  Celery 
and  lobster  black  bean  or  onion  with 
cauliflower  -  tomato  with  lamb  chops. 

Slip  your  hand  inside  a  waxed  sandwich 
bag  and  you  have  a  perfect  mitt  for 
greasing  your  baking  pans  and  casserole 
dishes. 

To  reheat  roast,  wrap  in  aluminum  foil 
and  heat  in  a  slow  oven. 

Hard  boiled  eggs  will  peel  easily  when 
cracked  and  placed  in  cold  water  immedi- 
ately after  taking  out  of  the  hot  water. 

You  can  cut  a  meringue  pie  cleanly  by 
coating  both  sides  of  the  knife  lightly  with 

butter. 

When  recipe  calls  for  adding  raw  eggs  to 
hot  mixture,  always  begin  by  adding  a 
small  amount  of  hot  mixture  to  the  beaten 
eggs  slowly  to  avoid  curdling. 

To  remove  fish  odor  from  hands,  utensils 
and  dish  cloths,  use  one  teaspoon  baking 
soda  to  quart  of  water. 

To  keep  icings  moist  and  to  prevent 
cracking,  add  a  pinch  of  baking  soda  to 
the  icing. 

If  soup  tastes  very  salty,  a  raw  piece  of 
potato  placed  in  the  pot  will  absorb  it. 

Pour  water  into  mold  and  then  drain 
before  pouring  in  mixture  to  be  chilled. 
Will  come  out  of  mold  easier. 

When  rolling  cooky  dough,  sprinkle 
board  with  powdered  sugar  instead  of 
flour.  Too  much  flour  makes  the  dough 
heavy.  When  freezing  cookies  with  a 
frosting,  place  them  in  freezer  un- 
wrapped for  about  2  hours  -  wrap  without 
worrying  about  them  sticking  together.

HOT  ORANGE  JUICE  PUNCH 


3  cans  (small)  frozen  orange 

juice 
9  cans  water 
1/2  c.  ReaLemon  juice 
2  qt.  apple  cider 


2  whole  sticks  cinnamon 
8  to  10  whole  cloves 

1  1/2  c.  sugar 

2  oranges,  cut  into  cart 
wheels 


Place  2  oranges,  spices  and  sugar  in  a  large  saucepan  with 
enough  water  to  cover.  Bring  to  boiling  point.  Remove  spices  and  add 
other  juices.     Make  hot  but  don't  boil.    This  makes  30  small  cups. 

Polly  Mabry 

ORANGE  MINT  JULEP 


2  (6  oz.)  cans  frozen  orange 

juice 
1  c.  fresh  chopped  mint 
1  c.  sugar 


14  oz.  sparkling  water  or 

ginger  ale 
1/2  c.  lime  juice 


Reconstitute  juice.  Heat  2  cups  juice  and  bring  to  boil, 
watching  carefully  to  prevent  boil  over.  Combine  mint  and  sugar  and 
mash  in  a  small  bowl  with  fork.  Pour  hot  juice  over  mint.  Let  set 
until  cool.  Strain,  discarding  mint.  Add  remaining  orange  juice  and 
lime  juice.  Chill.  Add  ginger  ale  or  sparkling  water  just  before 
serving.     Serve  over  ice.     Yields  8  servings. 

Gail  T.  Bunn 

CREAMY  HOT  CHOCOLATE  MIX 


6  oz.  powdered  creamer 
1/2  c.  powdered  sugar 
8  qt.  size  powdered  milk 


2  lb.  box  chocolate  flavored 
drink  mix 


Mix    all    ingredients    thoroughly    and    store    in    an    airtight    contain- 
er.    Use  1/3  cup  mixture  in  a  cup  and  finish  with  boiling  water. 

Sam  Ussery

VEGETABLE  SANDWICHES 

1  large  carrot  1  envelope  unflavored  gelatin 

1  small  onion  1  c.  mayonnaise 

1  cucumber,  peeled  salt  to  taste 

1  pepper 

Grate  all  the  vegetables.  Squeeze  them  to  remove  as  much  juice 
as  possible.  Mix  2  tablespoons  juice  with  envelope  of  gelatin.  Put 
into  a  small  container  and  melt  over  hot  water.  Add  vegetables  to 
gelatin  mixture.  Fold  in  mayonnaise  and  add  salt.  Use  to  make  sand- 
wiches or  with  crackers. 

Mary  Ethel  Clayton 

CROCK-POT  APPLE  BUTTER 

12  c.  cooked  apples,  puree  1/2  c.  cinnamon  hots 

until  smooth  1/2  c.  vinegar 

6  c.  sugar 

Put  applesauce  in  pot  on  high.  Cook  down  for  3  hours.  Add 
sugar  and  vinegar.  Cook  6  hours.  Then  add  cinnamon  hots  and  cook 
until  thick.  Be  sure  to  cook  with  lid  on,  but  place  6  or  8  paper 
towels  under  lid  to  collect  steam. 

Ella  H.  Maner 

EGG  CASSEROLE 

6  hard-boiled  eggs  1/2  c.  milk 

2  Tbsp.  finely  chopped  onions  2  c.  crushed  potato  chips 
1  can  mushroom  soup 

Slice  hard-boiled  eggs.  Place  in  shallow  baking  dish  and 
sprinkle  with  finely  chopped  onions.  Mix  soup  with  milk  and  pour  over 
eggs  and  onions.  Top  with  crushed  potato  chips.  Bake  35  minutes  in 
350°  oven. 

Miriam  J.  Sims

MUSHROOM  PILAF 


1  stick  butter  or  margarine 
1  1/2  c.  rice  (regular) 
1  can  beef  consomme  soup 
1  can  onion  soup 


2  lb.  fresh  mushrooms, 

cleaned,  trimmed  and  sliced 
1  c.  cheese 


Melt  butter  in  2-quart  casserole  in  oven.  Stir  rice  in  to  coat. 
Add  other  ingredients  except  cheese.  Stir  well.  Cover  and  bake  55

minutes  before  done,  cover  with  1  cup  cheese.

BARLEY  CASSEROLE 

1/2  c.  butter  or  margarine  1  (3  oz.)  can  drained  sliced 

1  c.  quick-cooking  fine  barley  or  chopped  mushrooms  or  3/4 

1  medium  onion,  chopped  c.  fresh  mushrooms  sauteed 

1  (2  oz.)  dehydrated  onion  in  a  little  butter 

soup  mix  1  (5  oz.)  can  sliced  water 

2  c.  chicken  broth  chestnuts,  drained 

1/2  c.  slivered  almonds 

Saute  barley  and  onion  until  golden  in  color.  Stir  frequently. 
Combine  soup  mix  and  chicken  broth.  Add  rest  of  ingredients  to  barley 
and  stir  well.  Turn  into  casserole  (about  a  9  x  12-inch  size).  Cover 
and  bake  at  350°  for  1  hour,  adding  more  liquid  if  needed. 

This  can  be  prepared  a  day  ahead  of  time  and  refrigerated.  If 
you  do  store,  you  will  need  to  add  more  liquid.  Homemade  chicken  broth 
is  best.  If  use  a  prepared  canned  soup  such  as  Campbell's,  be  sure  to 
dilute  with  an  equal  amount  of  water.  If  prepared  soup  isn't  concen- 
trated, probably  won't  need  extra  water. 

Jo  Avett

TERMS  USED  IN  COOKING 

APPETIZER  —  A  small  serving  of  food  served  before  or  as  the 

first  course  of  a  meal. 

ASPIC  —  A  transparent  jelly,  usually  meat,  which  has  been 

boiled  down  to  become  firm  when  cold. 

BATTER  —  A  mixture  of  flour  or  liquid  that  can  be  beaten  or 

stirred. 

BISQUE  —  A  rich  thick  cream  soup  made  from  fish. 

BLANCH  —  To  place  fruits  or  nuts  in  boiling  water  to  remove 

skins,  also  to  dip  vegetables  in  boiling  water  in  preparation  for 

freezing,  canning  or  drying. 

BOUILLABAISE  —  A  chowder  made  from  several  varieties  of 

fish  and  wine. 

BOUILLON  —  Clear  soup  made  from  lean  beef. 

BRAISE  —  To  brown  meat  or  vegetables  in  hot  fat,  then  to  cook 

slowly  in  small  amount  of  liquid. 

CARAMEL  —  Burnt  sugar  syrup  used  for  coloring  and  flavoring. 

Also  a  chewy  candy. 

CHICORY  —  A  plant  root  that  is  cut  into  slices,  dried  and  roasted 

into  coffee.    The  plant  leaves  are  used  for  salad  and  sometimes 

called  curly  endive. 

CIDER  —  The  juice  from  pressed  apples  used  as  a  beverage  or  to 

make  vinegar. 

CLARIFY  —  To  make  a  liquid  clear  by  adding  beaten  egg  white 

and  egg  shells.   The  egg  coagulates  in  hot  liquid  and  cloudiness 

adheres  to  it.   The  liquid  is  then  strained. 

COBBLER  —  A  fruit  pie  with  a  rich  biscuit  dough  made  in  a 

deep-dish. 

COCKTAIL  —  An  appetizer  served  before  or  as  the  first  course  of 

a  meal.    An  alcoholic  beverage  served  before  the  dinner  or  cut 

shellfish  with  tart  sauce  served  at  the  start  of  a  meal. 

CRACKLINGS  —  Crisp  particles  left  after  fat  has  been  fried  out. 

CROQUETTES  -  Chopped  meat  held  together  by  eggs,  shaped 

and  dipped  into  crumbs  then  fried. 

DOUGH  —  A  mixture  of  flour,  liquid  that  is  stiff  enough  to  be 

kneaded. 

DRIPPINGS  —  Liquids  resulting  from  meat  being  cooked. 

ENTREE  —  A  dish  served  between  the  chief  courses,  before  the 

roast. 

FONDUE  —  A  dish  made  of  cheese,  eggs,  etc. 

■s — ^t      »»      ans      »■?       o      act         ■  ■■       ^ 

Helpful  Cooking  Hints 


IF 


—  *•  1Z  ^g  3DC  ^g  ag  'J^  -  — 


" 


FRITTERS  —  Vegetables  or  fish  covered  with  butter  then  fried  in 

deep  fat. 

FROSTING  —  A  sugar  that  has  been  cooked  and  used  to  cover 

cakes,  and  other  foods. 

GIBLETS  —  The  liver,  gizzard  or  heart  of  poultry. 
]     HORS  d'OEUVRES—  Tart,   salty  or  crisp  foods   served  as 

appetizers. 

J    INFUSION  —  Liquid  taken  from  tea,  herbs  or  coffee. 
\    JULIENNE  —  Food  cut  into  very  thin  strips. 

MACEDOINE  —  A  mixture  of  fruits  or  vegetables. 

MARINATE  —  To  let  foods  stand  in  an  acid  mixture  of  oil  and 

vinegar,  then  flavored  with  spices  and  herbs. 

MINCE  —  To  cut  foods  in  very  fine  pieces. 

FOOD  PROCESSES 

BAKE  —  To  cook  by  dry  heat,  usually  in  an  oven. 
4    BARBECUE  —  To  roast  or  broil  whole,  as  a  hog,  fowl,  etc. 

Usually  done  on  a  revolving  frame  over  coals  or  upright  in  front  of 

coals.    To  cook  thin  slices  of  meat  in  a  highly  seasoned  vinegar 

sauce. 

BOIL  —  To  cook  in  liquid,  usually  water,  in  which  large  bubbles 

rise  rapidly  and  continually  so  that  all  the  liquid  is  agitated. 

BOILING  POINT  —  The  temperature  reached  when  a  mixture 

maintains  a  full  bubbling  motion  on  its  surface. 

BREW  —  To  cook  in  hot  liquid  until  flavor  is  extracted. 

BROIL  —  To  cook  by  exposing  the  food  directly  to  the  heat. 

BRAISE  —  To  cook  meat  by  searing  in  fat,  then  simmering  in  a 

covered  dish  in  small  amount  of  moisture. 
\    CANDY  —  To  conserve  or  preserve  by  boiling  with  sugar.    To 

incrust  or  coat  with  sugar. 
J    COAT  SPOON  —  When  a  mixture  forms  a  thin  even  film  on  the 
'     spoon. 

CODDLE  —  To  cook  slowly  and  gently  in  a  liquid  just  below  the 

boiling  point. 

CREAM  —  To  work  foods  until  soft  and  fluffy.  Usually  applied  to 

shortening  and  sugar. 

CUBE  —  To  cut  in  even  sliced  pieces. 
^    CUT  —  To  divide  foods  with  a  knife  or  scissors. 

DICE  —  To  cut  into  small  cubes. 

DISSOLVE  —  To  pass  into  solution. 
^    FOLD  —  To  combine,  using  a  motion  beginning  vertically  down 

through  the  mixture,  continuing  across  the  bottom  of  the  bowl 

and  ending  with  an  upward  and  over  motion.

MEATS,  POULTRY,  AND  SEAFOOD 

i                                                                                                                                                                            p 

Meats  are  a  substantial  part  of  all  homemakers  shopping  bill. 

Every  meal  should  be  planned  very  carefully  and  the  best  possible 

*    cut  of  meat  for  your  money  should  be  selected.    The  following      * 

chart  should  help  you  in  not  only  selecting  the  best  cut  of  meat, 

recommended  by  the  U.S. Department  of  Agricult 

ure  cutting 

|    chart 

,,  but  also  the  proper  amount  of  meat  to  serve.

VEGETABLE 


WAYS  TO 
PREPARE 


COOKING 


TIME 


Asparagus 


Wash;  gently  scrub 
with  vegetable 
brush.  Break  the 
stalks.  They  will 
snap  where  tender 
part  starts. 


Cook  coverd  in  small 
amount  of  boiling 
salted  water. 

Cut  up 

Whole  spears 


8-10  mins. 
10-15  mins. 


Beans, 
green  or  wax 


Wash;  remove  ends 
and  strings.  Cut  in  1- 
inch  pieces,  leave 
whole,  or  slit 
lengthwise. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water. 


20-30  mins. 


Navy  Beans, 
dried 


Rinse.  Soak  over- 
night in  3  times  as 
much  water  as 
beans;  OR  bring  to 
boil,  simmer  several 
minutes  and  let 
stand  1  hour  or 
more. 


Cover  and  simmer  in 
water  used  for 
soaking.  Add  salt. 


1  !4  hours 


Beets 


Cut  off  all  but  1  inch 
of  stems  and  root; 
wash  and  scrub 
thoroughly.  Do  not 
pare. 


Cook  covered  in 
boiling  salted  water. 
Peel  when  done. 


35-60  mins. 


Broccoli 


Remove  tough  part 
of  stalks  and  outer 
leaves.  Split  rest  of 
stalk  almost  to 
flowerets;  OR  Cut  in 
1  -inch  pieces; 
separate  stalks  from 
flowerets. 


Tie  stalks  in  bundles 
using  folded  strips  of 
foil.  Cover,  cook 
standing  up  in 
boiling,  salted  water. 
Cook  pieces  covered 
in  boiling  salted 
water  to  cover  5  to  8 
mins.;  add  flowerets. 


15-20  mins. 


10-15  min. 
Total 


Brussels 
Sprouts 


Wash  thoroughly; 
cut  off  wilted  leaves. 
If  large  Brussels 
sprouts,  cut  in  half 
lengthwise. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  waited  water. 


10-15  mins. 


Cabbage, 
green 


Wash;  remove 
wilted  outer  leaves. 
Cut  in  6  to  8  wedges; 
OR  shred. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water. 


10-12  mins.    J 
Wedges 


Carrots 


Wash,  scrape  or 
pare.  Slice,  cut  up  in 
quarters  or  strips,  or 
leave  whole. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water 
or  in  consomme. 


20-25  mins. 
Whole      b 


Cauliflower 


l 


Remove  leaves  and 
some  of  the  woody 
stem.  Leave 'whole 
or  separate  into 
flowerets. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water. 


20-25  mins. 

Whole 
15-20  mins. 
Flowerets

Table  For  Cooking  Vegetables 


VEGETABLE 


WAYS    TO 
PREPARE 


COOKING 


TIME 


Celery 


Scrub  thoroughly. 
Cut  off  leaves  and 
trim  roots.  Slice  into 
desired  lengths. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water 
or  in  consomme. 


10-15  mins. 


Corn 


Remove  husks  and 
silks  from  fresh  corn. 
Rinse  and  cook 
whole. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water; 
OR  cook  uncovered 
in  enough  boiling 
salted  water  to  cover 
ears. 


6-8  mins. 


Eggplant 


Wash.    If    skin    is 
tough,  pare.  Cut  in 

V?  -inch  slices. 


Dip  in  beaten  egg, 
then  in  fine  dry 
bread  crumbs. 
Brown  slowly  on 
both  sides  in  hot  fat. 
Season. 


Approx. 
4  mins. 


Mushrooms 


Wash;  cut  off  tips  of 
stems.  Leave  whole 
or  slice. 


Add  to  melted  butter 
in  skillet;  sprinkle 
with  flour  and  mix. 
Cover  and  cook 
slowly,  turning  oc- 
casionally. 


8-10  mins. 


I- 


Okro 


Wash  pods;  cut  off 
stems.  Slice  or  leave 
whole. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water. 


8-15  mins. 


Parsnips 


Wash  thoroughly; 
pare  or  scrape.  Slice 
lengthwise  or 
crosswise. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water. 


15-20  mins. 


Peas,  Green 
Spmaci 


Shell  and  wash. 


Cook  covered  in 
small  amount  of 
boiling  salted  water. 


8-15  mins. 


Spinach 


Cut  off  roots  and 
wash  several  times 
in  lukewarm  water, 
lifting  out  of  water 
as  you  wash. 


Cook  covered 
without  adding 
water.  Reduce  heat 
when  steam  forms. 
Turn  often  while 
cooking. 


3-5  mins. 


Zucchini 


Wash;  do  not  pare. 
Slice  thin. 


Season  and  cook 
covered  in  butter  in 
skillet  for  5  mins. 
Uncover  and  cook 
till  tender,  turning 
slices. 


10  mins. 
Total 


Tomatoes 


Wash       ripened 
tomatoes. 


Cook  slowly, 
covered  without  ad- 
ding water. 


10-15  mins. 


sac

SUBSTITUTIONS   FOR   INGREDIENTS 


1  tablespoon  cornstarch  (for  thickening)  ....  2  tablespoons  flour 

1  cup  sifted  cake  flour  ....  1  cup  minus  2  tablespoons  sifted 

all-purpose  flour. 

1  cup  sour  milk  ....  1  cup  sweet  milk  into  which  1  tablespoon 

vinegar  or  lemon  juice  has  been  stirred. 

1  square  chocolate  (1  ounce)  ....  3  or  4  tablespoons  cocoa  plus  1/2 

tablespoon  fat. 

1  cup  sifted  all-purpose  flour  ....  1  cup  plus  2  tablespoons  sifted 

cake  flour. 

1  cup  sweet  milk  ....  1  cup  sour  milk  or  buttermilk  plus  1  /2 

teaspoon  baking  soda. 

1  cup  cream,  sour,  thin  ....  3  tablespoons  butter  and  3/4  cup  milk 

in  sour  milk  recipe. 

1  whole  egg  ....  2  egg  yolks  for  custards. 

1  cup  molasses  ....  1  cup  honey. 

1  package  active  dry  yeast  ....  1  cake  compressed  yeast. 

1  tablespoon  instant  minced  onion,  dehydrated....  1  small  fresh 

onion. 

1  tablespoon  prepared  mustard  ....  1  teaspoon  dry  mustard.
